When solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which is in the stomach and in the intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by means of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of great virtue, then do one great cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle to each cautery clavile subtle, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the thigh, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, because the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are or at the foundation, or one or more, and are old and are of large humors cold and moist corrupted, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, if you make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is all outside below the almecdate poc and poc in triangulating, and one cautery below the buttock; two fingers.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face one places one large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and one other on the liver, and one other on the mouse to all the cautery clavile; and let the cautery be open long time. After cure the place as long as it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnosity that is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut thelul, then heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then put it all ablaze on top of that thelul cut; and let it there as long as your hand  that the cauteries comes to the birth of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this one or two times, and if there is much thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after cure with ointments beneficial as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchatim, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure incision or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes such a malady that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to any person, and is filled and surrounded with putrefaction and corrupt moisture, then you must first probe it carefully with a subtle probe, and guard that you know the depth of the probe. After this, apply the cautery which resembles .i. razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and restart the cautery until the flesh putrid and corrupt is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity needed; and guard yourself from burning the nerves which are there, and the large veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestine, then guard yourself from these areas, and only do this in the fleshy part, and think that it is not pierced; after healing the area until it is sound, and if the area is sealed, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the area is healed entirely; and if the materials are not removed, know that the area is diseased, and the bones at the base are corrupt; and thus as one of these which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the malady of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes with great windiness, and does not take root in woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the loins on one side and the other with the cautery of the clavicle that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, then there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will give more aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then I make a cautery in the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as my thumb; and I make one cautery outside the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauteries be clavicle-shaped according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the marshes
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marshes are cold and moist, and do not allow for this to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the bud, as we have said of the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries above the back; and let the cautery be clavil, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the bone of the hip, and for this cause it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found the location of the viscus department, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the bone of the hip with one cautery seeming to a circle, and mark before the location around the bone as it turns, so that the bone be inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as that used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make iii. cauteries of the olive large, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all the others; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After this, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, together with hot medicines, and cautery by fire. Cautery by fire is according to many manners, some of which are such: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them good depth and large, and have between each cautery a space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the top of the hip, so there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, so the cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do in such manner that the circles contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then one makes two cauteries there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, at the left part a point; and let the cautery be cuticular, and let the thickness of the heart be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the foot or near it, then he cauterizes where he feels the pain three points or four with the cautery which is called 'point'.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then one makes more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then one makes a cautery with the cuticular or circular cautery, and be well warned in all your cauteries that you do not leave so much of the cautery that you burn the nerves and the great arteries, and that you do no more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have cauterized on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot. After a belly discharge from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in 2 parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. // And the wise said in the cautery of the hip, because of what follows here is the manner, make 1 such iron and be at the head also as large as a thimble of finger, or a little less, and be by entrechetres and be from one entrechetres to the other with space the quantity of a knuckle of the thumb; and let the entrechetres be toward 2 parts, and let them be also like nuts, and there be 1 hinge of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and feels hot, and then put it on the bone of the sick hip, and be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once 1 cautery reont and let it lie for 3 days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound covered for a long time; after the cure of oiling until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and nevertheless those are good cauteries, which can endure it, and where it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or by too great evacuation, or by similar appearance of cold expanded matter, none of these appearances are worth cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It behooves after these things that the patient is void of fetid pills or other similar ones, that one makes on his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with incisions, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery that is called 'point'; and if you see, make three or four cauteries at the clavi middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow spine when they are lying down, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this kind according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery pricks each part of the spine equally. And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with the cautery prick .ii. lines or .iij., and let the points be near each other. After curing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring the cautery to a gangrened spot which is in the spame of the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the wise call "podagra" properly, and when it is from cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the foot, then you make cautery to the whole cautery which one calls "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then you make cautery on each knee 3 or 4 cauteries of each part, with all the cautery olive-shaped; and if you have need of more, then you make more, but do not hold your hand further than while the head of the cautery is burning.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the wrist 2 lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the hips or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good government for the patient and prescribe medicines. For if you do good government for him and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in the angles, and the boils descend to the hips and it is new, so that when you see him healed, he does not move that day; and that he uses things that lie on his belly, so that the fiends descend from his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his wing as long as the boils are repaired, and bring them to your heels, and mark with fire beneath the rupture over the bone of the fist, and all a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and it feels tender. Then bring the boils back to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return backward; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put below him one cushion and one sergeant on the thighs, and one other on the leg that holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, redo it again until you come to the bone; and be careful that the boil does not jump when you do the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or any other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And knows that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and of large people also great according to their measure; after .iij. days cure their place of the cautery of butter until the burning is removed; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and lie the patient .xl. days on his back until the wound is well joined; and it is necessary that his dressings be left long, so that the boil do not come out when he will go to bed in chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after .xl. days, when he wants to get up, if he is given a well-made splint and wear it for another .xl. days; and have good rest, that he does not work much and keeps himself from too much drinking and eating, and from too high laughter; and when he follows this instruction he will be healed completely. And I will say here after the cure of tailoring in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then you make one cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and be it at the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients said that one must cauterize with three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first sign the place of the rupture and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another outside, and hold your hand amidst all the cautery. But the first cauteries are lighter and more modest.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not avail, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called “poins,” and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsions and of its pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, it is well; if it does not, begin another cautery on top of that one, because such is the custom that it must move to the member that is closest to it, so it is necessary that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is not healed.
de meselerie	of meselary
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The meselary are aided at times by cautery with great help, and also the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. As soon as you see it being cauterized, take heed if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the entire patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the haiterel; and let your hand rest so that the cauteries reach to the bone, and as far as the escorces come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the mice according to what is written before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly felt, it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cautery tools that we have said or chief, and 1 cautery in its neck, and 2 cautery on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauterys on the spine of the back, and 1 large one on the hip and another near, and 2 on the 2 shoulders; and 2 on the knees, and 2 on the tendons of the thigh, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard yourself from the nerves that are on the last calf, so that you do not burn them; and at no time is cauterization made on the bone of the thumb, and 1 other on the bone of the stomach, and 1 other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when more cauteries are made, the more help is done, and it benefits; and know that the sick person does not feel any pain from the cautery as much as a healthy person feels it, because the body is already totally corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in manners of irons. After curing the place with flour of chickpeas mixed with honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	of inflammation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point going into the thickness of the flesh; then cure with dressings until it is healed. And sometimes one makes cauteries on the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that numbs the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and nonetheless let no one interfere unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of  albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness that is called “albaras” is present, and the means of medicine are of no avail, then cauterize with a cautery a point in depth, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, until the blanching is removed, and its color has changed; then cure with flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alder, of each one part; and be mixed all together, and be bound with a cloth, and be aerated in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of an ulcer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When an ulcer comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, if you cauterize it with the cautery which seems .i. circle, all around the tour of the ulcer.  And although some sages say that one should cauterize also in the middle of the ulcer; and yet this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it happen any time; and more right thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a sickness that is called "adubelati", and it delays dying or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the water of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see it hasten to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; after let it be as it is. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it inspected with the whole cautery, so heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this sickness called "adubelati" until the cautery pierces the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it from outside in such a manner that the course of the rot is lightened. After the cure as long as it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another kind of sickness called "corrodens", which is nothing else than a corruption of the limb, because it consumes the limbs like dry fire consumes the tendons. If you see this sickness in a place where it can suffer cauterization with both fire and iron, then sharpen small and large cautery irons, according to what is suitable for the place where the sickness is; after which cauterize all around until you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that all that is corrupted be removed. And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places softened broths with oil until the scabs from the fire are removed, and all the corruption. Then apply a cure of ointment-generating flesh. And if after three days you see that healthy flesh is not being born, it is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery on what remains corrupted. This corruption has sometimes been cured by aguie medicine in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for aguie medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the tendons that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that at the feet by fire there is born a sickness which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing of bad fortune that bleaches the foot. And the cauteries for this sickness are thus in .ij. manners. It's to know cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. Cautery of fire is that you heat one cautery pointed like as it is a quill of vulture, and be made of good iron at the measure that it can bend the nail on all sides, and that it have subtle margins; after put it all hot upon the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and let it thus for .iij. days until it begins to fester rot; then I make a poultice of wild mallows ground with wool, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and will be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment enjaring flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happens and in hands and in feet, it is fitting that you bring them cautery of hot water; and it is in this manner: take a chain of iron or iron, or a quill of vulture, and put on the nail and the other side, that is to say tendons warts; and put the chain so that it encircles all around, then I put a pot of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water way deep until the root; and let the patient one hour the burning of the hot water; then leave him thus, and it will be uprooted from all its roots. Thus do another one after the other, as long as you uproot all those that are in the body, then cure them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or from quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you make for him 4 cauteries or 4 on the spine of the back, 1 cautery between each spine; and 1 cautery or weight, and 1 on the stomach at the olive cautery; so let the trembling leave, and hasten the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of bursting pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes appearing by fire the body bathes, or bursting pustules, which come from large corrupted matters. So it is fitting at first when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that the point is grasped by the fire, or of long aristolochia root, or the lentil-shaped cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from them forward, but are broken down the superfluities from which they come, and they are healed; but it is fitting that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to prolong.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it very hard until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no more drops issue; then put olive cauteries, several small and large ones, onto the fire until they are all red; then take one, or a large one or a small one according to the wound and its location where the artery is cut, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily another one of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to make these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that another malice does not come upon the patient; and know that when a vein departs from the artery, it cannot be well stretched even when the artery is large, unless by one of the .iiij. ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying of thread, or by medicines put upon which have power to stretch a vein; and be bound and strained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will bring about a tightening of the binding, or tight bandage with strips or to put fiery things upon, or other similar things, if it does not profit them not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has not medicine present, then he must put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bind tightly until it is stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the band, but moisten with cold water often that be very cold until the vein is congealed and thickened and stretched; and make then those things which he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of tail
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all illnesses where it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I put that chapter from the head to the feet, and I will in this chapter by the same way for those who more easily find what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, it is necessary, dear student, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary to take more great care.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. Because many kinds of people come to cures. Some come so sick with their malady that they die easily because of the foolishness they find in their illness, and of the greatness of their wickedness; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give you their senses, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is deceitful. It does not become you that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more care in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have taken and praised; and use divination and indication in the cures of your sick so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of length.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and rightness, and if you want to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in devising by chapters, according to those that it is before or chapter of cauteries, that I have devised them from the head to the feet, for those that you find more easily those that you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes many times to children at birth, and when the delivery is too strong the head of the child; and some times it comes from a cause unknown which one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and to all those that I have seen it hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better for me to leave the work on such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of whom the shoulder was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not bear it; and so much moisture had gathered that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you open the head with a wide incision; and be as long as two thumbs, as much as the moisture goes; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the head open from each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not return to you: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract the moisture entirely outwards. After, extract the fissures of linen and powders, and put wine and oil there, and leave it so until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with tents and ointments, and leave the chief bandage to be tightened, and afterwards feed the patient dry meat from the source of moisture until the limb is fortified and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you watch where the greatness of the abscess opens, and the assembly of the water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the water, and follow it according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and vein blood flows, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of summary
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a sickness called "catarrh" in the eyes or on the breast, and the sickness is old, and the cure of medicine does not profit, therefore the last cure is cauterizing with this one which one covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you want to cover them, that the patient recline his head; after which rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then restrain the patient's neck with one cloth; then look where the vein beats, and its sides on each side are after the ears, and so they are placed back; then sign the sides with ink, then cut both with a sharp spatula of two parts. Until the cut reaches the bone, and this be by the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula below the artery and cut it above, cutting also like two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood leaps out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at the touch, you must measure the quantity of the space of 3 fingers, then guide it and make it until the bone; and what is due to put out blood is 6 ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone with no sign of a scab, then cut it so that an abscess does not come, then restrain the wound and bind it, and the ointment cure until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and ancient soreness and similar things, and it is medicated by means of cures of medicine and all those do not benefit him, then we drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes rear the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned outside than in some men who are too cold; and if it is returned, he strains his neck from the patient with some cloths, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then draw it upward as with pincers, and depart well from the webs that are under each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it back to the point of the uncine, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two chies. For if it is not cut, it does not jump out all at once.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood of the six points, up to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double thread strong silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the soldering of the wound, and comes hemorrhage; then cut the superfluity which is between the two ties in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the cutellaire cautery up to the bone until the chies are cut; and this is the best work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is help to finish the moistures: for this reason it is of greater help to moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills their place with old cotton and puts on tents well made; and when they are untied, let them be covered with dry medicines which make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without cord of the artery as much as you work upon it, then hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place with vitriol and restrain it to your hand that the wound be stanched; and if you have not these things present, put on the place your finger until the bleeding ceases, and rise the place of cold water until the bleeding stops, and be restrained as it is necessary; and what is more mature and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenching of .ij. parts, but the trenchings be well spaced to keep longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too hard, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives one must of wide space, and then when you have signed of them the two points, and you place the burning iron over it until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two points; and be separated between the two shoulders because it is not joined of this cautery at all; and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from veins that are on the skin of the head's forehead, and it does not profit any medicine one makes, and you see the face of the patient become contorted, and feels on the forehead a walking as if of trembling; and where oil is being held and moist so that the hair of the eyebrows is falling, and the eyebrows are burned, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it by the ancients “a contused cure,” and you do to the patient who has this malady the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make three incisions in the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one incision be as two should entirely through the forehead down to the eyebrow, and the other two at the two ribs above the cheekbones; and guard yourself from the incision of the arteries that are at the two ribs above the cheekbones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe the blood, then put the spatula sharp on two parts so that its form is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is below the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the kernel that is between the two incisions to the entire surface that is on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract far this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is put into the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the sharp side toward the fleshy part to the heart, and the blunt side toward the bone, and push it as far as it comes to the middle fissure. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches that which opens to the heart, and then on the other side make in the middle fissure until the other edge; and then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened in wine and oil and asil, and keep that no abscess comes; and on the third day untie the linen, and there administer great quantities of lukewarm water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures which are used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come catarrh acute customarily, and you see the eyes sunk in and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in they do a pain acute, and the sick one sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh ne comes from many veins, and the change cure that is, so is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And is that you command to the patient to rear his forehead, then make a great fissure amidst the forehead, and another wide one. i. poc. And commence from the temple left to the temple right, and let the incision be unto the bone; and keep your hand from the nerves of the temples which move at the eating; and when the bone is uncovered, then wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the fissure and put there old cotton, and linen bandage; then tie above draping moistened in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscess; when it is removed, then it behooves you to rub the bone until flesh begins to come forth, then cure with drying things, that they cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such manner: take .ij. parts of flower of wheat, and .iiij. parts of colofine, and make thereof a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to cause flesh to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or stone or semblance such as iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing thing such as water and oil and semblance things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear a stone or another kind of thing that does not fit in the ear nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, instill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and have him sneeze with condiment, and stop his nostrils when sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. Many times it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with fine tweezers, for that is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine, double-edged needle; and if it does not come out by this, make a cane of iron and thrust the head of the cane or puncture of the ear strongly, and stop those around the cane with soft wax so that no air can enter there with the cane; then try to pull it out, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take a piece of glue that is used to catch birds, and put it on any instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a dab of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and try to pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not come out of all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to cut the ear thus as an abscess comes and spasms; and the manner of cutting it is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be like a crescent moon, as far as you come to the bone, then the bone according to your strength, and suck it diligently with your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with subtle pincers and sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the case where water falls into the ear, it behooves the patient to use externally of condis first, and ample the ear with old cotton. And let him lie on that same ear where the water is. If it goes out by this, it is good.
