If not, take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; and put them into the patient's ear where it hurts, and throw them up from his side with his feet; and make him do this of stone after stone until the water is all gone, and thus if it is all out; and if you see it, take one reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end catch fire until the best part of the reed is burnt; then make another piece of others until the water is gone completely, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, then administer the extraction with forceps; and this is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not help, then it behooves you to look at the ear in the sun: if there appears no worms, then you treat them with subtle forceps, and if they do not appear, then take the instrument of which this is the shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed forming at all the canine; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, so stop around the canine with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, so administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the killing of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and your medicines into the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or brass, narrow below to one little holes, and wide above to distill; and for pressing within the distillation one instrument of brass well made for this, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; then I throw your oil or your juice, and what you want from your medicines into the canine, and the canine be in the ear; then put within the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and feel the patient inside, and let the distillations one pock be warmed by the fire then one distills it into the ear; and keep that it be not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any holes in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by clogging of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes from deep within the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes they happen i.e. one point of fire, and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from deep within if one cannot see it, is of great damage in many dispositions, and in this, you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opening, then the work has all this spatula form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and trenchant in front and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh born or a part of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the boil is in the ear, then take one razor subtle and light and heat it a little to the fire, then put it where the ear's body.  If you feel the boil that the patient feels great pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and guard that you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole made, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this with no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you pull out the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the bleeding which are or treated by distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the skin of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althlul that comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, then it is necessary that you extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the cut off with a spatula from its roots; then put on their place powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorts, then cauterize them with the subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterization after incision is worth a move; and many times they return, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.
de la gresle	of the groin
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times in papers come to the eyes things that seem gravel in its shape and in its hardness, and for this reason is this disease called "grapes", and is an assembly of moisture large on the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the gravel moves from one side and the other, and this is a light thing to know; make then with the wide, then the peel of each part lightly, then take with the tweezers, and cut. If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit the paper, then it grieves nothing to the patient; and if the fissure is large, so assemble it with a stitch, and cure as long as it is healed; and if it is small, then do not make any force, because the healing restores it soon and prevents flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel is descending into the inside of the ear toward the top part, then turn over the paper, and being the gravel with tweezers, and cut it and press on one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the gravel is cut, let leave the eye of salty water, and cure the place from that which prevents flesh as long as the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is engendered in the tissues of the papers above, and this happens more to children than anyone else, and grieves them greatly at their eyes, and they come to have cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for that reason they lie down on their faces, and sleep so, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and the appearance has covered with exinach which opens in the eye. And when you press it with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of working it is that the patient puts his head on your thigh; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a spatula trenching a fissure of the width, and not be more than large as the wound made on the vein's opening; and making the skin in parts until you reach the exinach; and in many dispositions comes exinach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then with a whole piece of cloth between your fingers on the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and keep that you do not add in the fissure, that you do not reach all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, so gently widen the split until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and put them on top, and restrain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who grind flax and put it on top to corrupt the moisture that is lingering. Then treat it until it is healed. And if pus comes back hot to the site, then treat it with soothing ointments until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on papers hairs are born aligned other than the natural, and are grown, they harm the eyes, and bring manners of maladies as tears accustomed and softening of the papers and albuginea, until it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery entire fire, or by medicine ague according to what it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, it puts an needle to all .i. thread above; and let it be below the margin of the paper or where the hair grows near these hairs, and draw .i. thread to the top of the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the aligned hairs, to all the spatula, from the great tear to the small; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then lay on the paper a figure of enche, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it behooves that the figure be according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if a tail who needs one copes much quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; then make to all the spatula above the .ij. lines that you have signed, and begin from the great tear to the small; and let it be one of the clefts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the oncine in one of the .ij. angles of the heart, then exfoliate it all; then assemble the .ij. lips with a stitch of a needle to all .i. thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air the superfluity of threads above the .ij. eyebrows to no glutinous things, if you want to do this; and if not, have no care about it, then leave the stitch and the threads until .iij. days or .iiij.; then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, because the paper revives at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitching is muedre (as they said the ancients), and this work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another manner: and is that you signify the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at iii. ounces separated according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above the small strengths equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are not able to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle which has one thread, and put it into the figure; and put another thread alongside the large tear, and the second thread alongside the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin upon what you have signified, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then appease it with cerote and similar soothing ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use those that we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the cauteries is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and its make inside according to what I have said, and then make two cauteries by art, and two threads subtle also long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and cut the two heads from two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly upon those that summit over the paper of the eye, and strain the two cauteries of the two parts form; and let it thus for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and hold, as long as it seeks by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with more force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is soldered, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hair; and this is the form of the two cauteries that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and it puts 1 silk thread fine and subtle; then assemble the shoulders and knot them one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase another fine silken thread briefly, and knot the chief of the two threads; then put the patient's head on your healthy; and let it be towards the sun so that the work is clear, because it is a subtle and small work, then put the needle to all the chase into the root of the hair adjusted, and make it pierce the paper hastily until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there are 1 or 2 or 3 or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, so you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out from the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair hardens in its place and lets the flesh grow up; and if the hairs are small, accompany 1 long hair from the natural ones, and let it be raised with that one or you leave it, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this illness that is called “aleacrati” or rot comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it happens by sudden blow, or cut or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of treatment for this is that you cut the suture, and separate the eyelids, and put within wadding of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not proper that you use in its cure things that dry and restrain. For if you do so, the illness returns worse than the first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or althea and flax seed boiled, and diacoylon ointment melted in any of the oils, and envelop a wadding, and cure it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close according to the form it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing but a treatment for this illness, that it may not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness that is "axacrati", and it is truly called "swollen eye," and it is natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of working on it in this is that you take a needle, which has two threads, and put it into the flesh, and let it go through from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two sides of the flesh; then keep the flesh above the entire needle, and cut at one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the flesh returns according to what is right, it is good; if not so, then take one razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the skin, and make two incisions where there are edges inside the skin; and let the ends of the two incisions be at the two corners of the incision that you have cut, and make such angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has no "j" ; then remove that flesh, according to the amount that its edges are pushed downwards, from what follows the skin, then adjust the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat with those that we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a rupture or stitch or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain cut under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said above; then bind between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything of all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the sick man himself, according to what is necessary of work and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs to hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor make its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the while as pinches, until you cut what is attached to the spatula, subtle, which is not too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula be too sharp nor pierce the eye; and let your incision, with which you scrape together that assembly, be slight, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all that assembly, and do at no time in the eye salt water, and the lift of sweet water, and of collier; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in abundance of egg; and after the third day use the collier and things soothing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in .ii. manners: it is nervous and seeming to .i. hard syfac, and another which is not nervous but is seeming to white moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and one cuide panre as pinces, it cannot om; and the one and the other semblance commences towards the great tear, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then the one opens the eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as pinces with a small doubleure, and the one on top; then take a needle, and put in it .i. hair of horse, or calf, or ox, and .i. strong thread; and double the point of the needle a poc and place it into the angle, and pierce it through the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the one on top, and scrape at all the hair the side of the angle which follows the prunele and silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear to all the spatumile subtle and as small forces, and leave the flesh naturally or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears customarily; and no times is the angle on the one only, and to the thread, as we have said; then the scraping one has all the spatumile souef of this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a little bit of ground silk, and from the collar made of lead ore, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as it is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved, and you cannot push the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so operate on the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light point acute according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail up subtly, and if you see that it diminishes not and the reason hastens, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of lead ore and red collar and ground silk, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same operation, as long as it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no thing is contrary to you in the eye, such as an abscess of chaus, then milk it, and cure first the abscess hot until it be healed, then begin again the work as before, until it be healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh by the tear hurts in the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the bone and in cut a part and not half too, that body of tears doesn't come; then distill in the eye colic red which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are born at times red flesh, and covers the iris and restrains on the eyelids and turns them to the outside, and it seems like a rose of baume; and the work is that the patient puts his head in good health, then he operates the eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable instruments for this, and support it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go on cutting to the razor until the end, and keep you that you do not bleach the eye during the operation; and let the incision be of the spatula which we have said in the incision of the angle and the small forces of which one removes the sebum, as the form after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of seal ground or you distill red mercury and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil of fire cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be assured of a hot abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the sinew cover it, and you doubt a hot abscess, so leave the oil and cure the abscess of things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as long as flesh is joined in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you apply the cure of each weak oil from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member be undergoing that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Red veins that are covered over the eye, and they take away from sight their work and weaken the eye all days. It is necessary then for you first to look at the eye, in which one is, if it is, or not, and there is no other disease except the red vein; therefore the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your shoulder, then suspend those veins to the whole outline according to his wisdom, and let the outlines be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two outlines by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then the coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins out of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at the hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill in the eye green and red collyrium to corrode what is remained of the red vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of these in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and let it for some days until the pains are calmed and it is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and with medicine burning according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut into the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and the blackness, if the king has all the instruments of what here is the form; and it is called «aspre chief», and it is made of iron one head, and it is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little while you know that this corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal drying agents.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is soldered and there is no birth of pus, and the body of the bone is soldered, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not renew and is not an abscess, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, if there is another way than to bring the fistula back to its original opening according to this form: And it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be thinned to the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone below the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye  1 finger width, then turn to the whole forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his forehead; and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the places, so goes the matter to the forehead; thus it is lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open and throughout entirely, and nothing comes to disturb the forehead, nor diminishes, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal, then place suction cups or a halter without hurting for sucking, then put on the eye  1 layer made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster above with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one in 4, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye has need for; then strap it from above with a strong bandage, and restart the suction cups for sucking without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the layers soften, it is necessary that you tighten it very much; then remove the layer after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not; then restart the plaster and cloths and the layer and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the dislocaiton of a sleeve
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruption comes in the sleeve, then open it, and it comes out like a piece of resin, grain by grain, and is easy to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is one double thread from the lachrymal part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the vine around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put over the other eye half in a circle of an egg; and let him until the threads fall with the vine, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and any time the wound is restrained by the vine on each side by a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show a great appearance, then pierce them with a fine spatula that comes from the eye itself, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter into them immediately; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye cavity
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease which is called “alcunnati”  is nothing but the cavity of the eye assembled in the eye, seeming like a sharp descending, and it is not a sharp; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the sick person sit on i. a seat equipped and straight, then take the head between your hands of .ij. parts, and move it as much as you see the cavity coming upwards to your eyes; then be it fixed, and do not descend and let the light be scattered, and the sick person sees things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is sharp, and if the descent of the cavity is not equipped as we have said. so make the sick person sit between your hands, then take the small spatula and make on the cornea .i. pock by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the corona, as much as the cavity exits; and when it is exited, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then be cured of other cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's sharp points
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have seen the resemblances of needles in division, and those that are needed to pierce; so in work according to the health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie his healthy eye and hold it very firmly; then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if his eyes are left, or on your right hand if his eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if his eyes are left, the instrument that is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if his eyes are right; then place the point of the instrument near the crown by the width of a fingernail in that white part of the eye to the side of the tear duct, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and restore your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the end of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument until where the needle is, then express it down one way after another. If the needle sinks now, if he sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After repose .i. little, and if the eye returns the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ensfiched and it does not go up, si extract almagda lightly by turning your hand poc and poc; and then put back into the eye a point of silk gemme, and leave of those the eye inside. Then put on outside the eye stuffed or linen moistened in rose oil and in yolk of egg, and tie with the healthy eye. Nos, and those who are of our time, put upon coming broiet with yolk of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it is necessary that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit," of this it is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep in by force, but make .i. them subtle, then put almond, as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with .i. dorteur, where he sleeps on his back in .j. dark place; and be kept from all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in the same dark house, and examine his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do these after the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you align these, because the liquid mounts hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess comes from the eye, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and address it with those who soothe the abscess; and when it is calmed down, then untie the sight and put on his face .i. orilliet to cover any day, and be in the same dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and return to his things; and know that none of disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almond pierce, to which one sucks the liquid, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almonds, for those who do not know them see them; and they are properly of arrain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these be of the same subtlety, and the last in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh where the veins
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At no time do veins arise or join together in diverse ways, so that there are none that resemble scorpions with many legs; and if there are such ones where flesh is discolored, and if there is flesh of good color. In those of these veins which is smooth, and not discolored, it behoves you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and drop the ointment on those veins, and drive them outward; then cut what you can support with a subtle sharp spatula from one side, until you know that the flesh is all removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains that one cannot cover, open it completely, i.e., with subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without the swarm or abscess clothes, secure it as it is proper; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the blood is extinguished and all the pus is removed, then pour in water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the nose works and moisture comes as far as the mouth, know that it is sane; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so the instruments cannot come to cut; therefore it behooves you to put i. a thread of linen somewhat thick, and be wove by hands, and have between each knot a space of i. an inch or less; and place the patient's head with the thread into the nose at its tip, and pull gently until it comes out through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do the children in school this way, and it is easy for whoever wants to do it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other so long as they are which are or thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corroded all of the flesh; then pull out the threads, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back into the nose as before; do this for iij days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that is left of flesh; and then put on the nose a poultice of earth for some days until it is sane; and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, as a basin, and lead it thusly; and if you see fit, make a closed basin, and have the instruments clean for purging the head; and let it have one handle on the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone about the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the head of the bone a malady which is called "telul" is born, and grows and becomes great onwards, until it is visible to behold; and for this you should cut it at the beginning, and pull all out the bone, then put on its place the cautery or the burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is great, then take care if it is hard, of foul color, of poor feeling: if not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when one cuts it any time, it comes great misfortune to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touching, not of foul color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bone is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these working cartilages, it does little good, because in some men. Therefore, if this happens to any man, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a suture, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you should scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then join the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder over powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put over the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster that adheres, and leave it until it dries by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths there happen abscesses hard, resembling grains of sand, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cleave on each knot, and take with pincers and cut in each part; then apply to the place after incision of ground vitriol, until the blood be stanched; and then the ointment of oil, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is born on the gums flesh attached, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with pliers and cut it at its root, and leave to flow the pus or blood; then put on the place ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deaf people
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling; so you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs appearing, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and greenish color, and yellowness and other spots, as long as they are visible; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those not, then it begins again to scrape the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need different types of instruments to remove, according to what the work demonstrates to you, because the rasp used to remove outer teeth has other forms than that which removes between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to drain as much as you can, because one must not do otherwise; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to suck, it behooves you to be certain of the tooth aching. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks that it is a tooth sound, and draws the healthy tooth; yet nevertheless does not depart the pain from this, until the evil stays, because we have done this many times to our juniors; and when you are well certain of the tooth aching, it behooves you to scrape around the tooth at all its.  a spatula strong for guarding the gums on all sides; then move it with your two or tweezers subtle at the first point and point, until it is well loosened, then firmly affirm the tweezers; and let the head of the patient in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After you have extracted the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not jump free, then take any of these instruments and put it inside each side lightly, and move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and mixed, it behooves you to fill it with drapelz, where the perforations are; and restrain it subtly with tweezers, that it does not break when extracting; and it behooveth wisely to work around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. And beware that you do not do as ignorant elders do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break any time the chariot, and bring not what we have recounted; but often cause by the excision of this great sickness for the roots that remain there, or for the chariot that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine or oil and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, then apply to the place vitriol ground; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one must file teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be well-made iron, and be toothed for grip.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the tooth, it is necessary that you put on top of it cotton moistened with butter for one or two days, until the place is softened, then put the pliers called "algefri," so that the head resembles a careful beak; and inside they are made like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say a spatula, because of its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be it strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out by those means, it is good; if those do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which shape comes here:
