et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the direction of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles a large pair of tongs, of which shape comes here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it may not break, and know that many instruments are of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one breaks not a bone or other bones, or where it can be broken, then search for the instruments that you need, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, according to what is here the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for these, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in virgin women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or smooth it; therefore, the ray; and if it is with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to a small beak, and be of sharp iron at its summit:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cup is put and put in hands for several days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then the file of a kind of file as this is its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file that one makes needles with; and in filing the tooth little by little in several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plane at the end has no trace, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pricks the tongue, then it is necessary to file the roughness until it is equal, so that it does not prick the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front is dislocated, either by percussion or by a fall, and the patient cannot press on it so that it moves without pain, and you have cured it with medicines that restrain it, and this does not work; if this is the case, it is necessary to restrain it with a thread of gold, because the thread of silver becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes; and whether the thread is moderate or too large or too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth aligned, take the thread and loop it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the chies between the teeth, if there are one or more, as long as you wisely come to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the coverage again up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the chies of the thread with tweezers, and assemble them, and put them back between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue; then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, restrain it with another thread; if it remains, it will serve like this for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of aligning the two healthy teeth, and the two dislocated ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls, then it is put back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes the form of a tooth of bone of the vein is made, and it is put in the place where the deficiency is, and it is restrained as we have said, and remains and serves like this for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue or nature; or by accident of a sutured wound; and the work is such that you operate on the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament wide, until the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is due to the suture of a wound, then put the probe and cut widely that ligament; and guard that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is below; and when you have done so, lift the place with rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and apply it to the patient every night, so that the place cannot stitch. And if bleeding occurs, then put on the place powdered vitriol; and if the bleeding does not stop, then cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with other cures until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of rusty color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then touch it not, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiten, and there is moisture, then put in the probe, and make it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding does not stop at your work, then put on powdered vitriol until it is bleached, then return to your work until you extract all pus; then lift the place with vinegar and salt, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes comes from within the throat boils that are called «godath», and they call them properly the two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, so take care: if it is abscesses hard of small sense and of fusse color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the decorrement of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will part it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of blainche color reont, and the root is subtle, have appeared the instrument for covering, but first look whether the abscess chalz rests and is appeased. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his feet be in your health, and open the mouth and the preigne the serjans between his hands, and press the tongue down on all the instrument, of this is the form; and be of silver or of arrain subtle as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the abscess, so take the oncine and put it in the almond, and push it upwards more than you can; and do nothing of the cloths with, then the cope to the instrument, of this is the form, that seems ones forces; and nevertheless the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron inde or d’andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, so you cope it with pliers, of this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side, and the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient hot water, and water and thus, and if a discharge of blood happens, so gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound be cleansed; then cure it as long as it be healed; and at no time rise in the throat other abscesses than the two almonds, so cut them then just like the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I medicated a woman from an abscess that she had in her throat, which is to say one abscess of small size; and I had well closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit that was obstructed, and could not eat or drink, and would have died if she remained thus one day or two. And the abscess was so high that it had been put two fingers by the two openings where it came out. So I immediately, and placed in one a lance, then pulled out the pus, and in pulling a large portion of pus; then I refixed another in the other opening where it came out, and I opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after which I placed the lance into the abscess, and cut a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus was unblocked the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had evacuated, until it became very large; so I pierced it and cauterized it within the throat: thus remained without growing; and I left these parts, and do not know what God did to her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the grape is ripe and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is too large and round, it is called "grape". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pus of the abscess has subsided, and it is thin, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one that is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it. For there is great danger for the patient. It is therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned before; then put the needle in the grape, and pull it out, and cut it at one or two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves the voice, and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear to cut, then it is necessary that you use a certain thing to the cauterization of the senses of fear. And the manner of the cautery is acute sharp. And that the patient puts his head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue with the instrument which we have said or chapter of cautery, and confis with live very hot so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using the end of this instrument, from this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has or chief a hair where one puts the medicine, as like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle correct from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the palate; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it burning and the irritations of the medicine are appeased; and if you see it, take cotton and envelop it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the cavity above, until the cotton dries on the grape; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then leave it dry, and lie after four or five. And if you have need to restart the cautery of the medicine, start it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton buttered, and purify what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured by gargles as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put it therein, and make boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have one instrument hollowed according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or iron, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises to the ulcer through the pipe, until the ulcer is mortified; afterward resume often, until the ulcer dries, and guard that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this unless at the declination of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a pipe and put inside its head a piece of egg shell, so that the mouth of the sick person does not have too much heat; for the egg shell does not let the vapor heavily burden the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a thorn or fish spine gets lodged in the throat, or something else; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing. And what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it behooves you to make the sick person vomit thus as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the thing will be released by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will lodge itself, and then draw it out further; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take one instrument of wood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter into the throat, and have the head lifted high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come undone, nor put the bone inside; and it is better that the patient puts out the instrument, for he will know if the thing is blocked; so he pushes down, or he draws back the whole instrument equally until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	At no time is medicine used for bleeding as I have said in the division by the cure of medicines; and when these do not help, then look into the throat of the patient in the sun, after you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you. And if you see the bleeding, so treat it with all i. small tweezers, or fine forceps that are suited for this. And if these do not work, take a heated sheep's wool and put it into the throat of the patient, then put in the end of the sheep’s wool i. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient stays with thirst all day; then take full i. cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it inside without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the bleeding feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times because it will fall without suffering harm. And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot where there are burning coals, and let the bottom be covered with a thin cloth in the middle, and in that pierce the head of the instrument; then put your fumigation in, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes to his gums; and the gums will now fall, and if it does not fall, begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary that it will be cured by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the gums is, when one can see it, like tongs bent so as to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has asperities of lime, so that when it takes hold, it cannot let go; and behold here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscesses are, according to what the memory comes here after from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in .ij. manners which one is in its own semblance, and of those that it holds moisture. And the second manner is for the places where they are on the body. Because the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the body is mature according to its completion; and if some such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses which are near joints. Because when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it as long as it is full of pus, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which reason it is a cause of contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, then pierce it thus when it is ripe; and it is not necessary that you pierce an abscess ripe without digestion completed, except for that which is near the foundation, lest it should grow too wide, and be lengthened within, and there comes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the fever has decreased, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and of the swelling and softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more depends the place of the abscess, and where it opens pus; and be the perforation long in the body, and whether the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equal places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these that are swollen, according to the member itself. And when an abscess is in its place charnel, it is worth while you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, it will lengthen the body of the venom from it, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of it. And if an abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the member has need for. And it befits you to bring in small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the semblance of the greatness of the abscess; and if an abscess that it befits to cover the heart, and to cover; when it is become as .i. drapelets, and is softened, then it befits to do as one does with buboes: and if there are those that are cut in .iij. angles, and if there are those that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the angres; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and semblance cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no chief, as a superficial abscess, it befits you to pierce it plainly; and it befits when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then plug the abscess until the other day, then draw out nothing directly; do this many times of great to great, until the pus is all gone; also if the patient is of feeble virtue, or a woman carrying, or a small child, or old men decrepit. For the spirits are put in danger at every time with the issue of the pus, that by chance the patient might die, and you should not be concerned about it. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, then bring tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, it befits that you put in each one a tent so that it comes against the other; and if you have covered part of the skin in the abscess, and you have covered it around, then it befits that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen rags without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove the plug, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold and sharp water, and moisten one drapelet, and put it on the bleeding place many times. And if the bleeding persists, then bring governance and cure, and the powders that I have said in this book; and if it is in winter's time, and the place where the abscess is is very nervous, then it befits that you put on tents and drapelets moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is charnel, then it befits that you put on drapelets moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it befits, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of sores
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the boil on the pus-filled abscess and moist one is lighter because it has little blood. And in some of these abscesses or chief where there is no moisture, and from these I ones that I opened on a woman's head; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and cannot break; and if one had made any of it, one would have done to it as well as a wound like a stone. In other abscesses coming or chief, which come at the root of children and ears, the opening should always be at its lowest point so that the pus may flow out easily; and the cure as is proper.
des scrophules	Of the scrofulous
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come from other parts or of the body, and are many, and are joined together one with another. And each scrofulous is properly within its own part, as well as the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrophules are many. There are some that contain moisture, and some which are malignant who do not want to obey health. In that one therefore that you see of good disposition upon touching, and is similar in color to the flesh, and mute from each part and is not at all near to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; then it behooves you to open it from above, and to scrape it from each side, and make the two lips of the heart as one, if you have need for it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not be too much with the spatula or trenching, so that your hand escapes, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, so put in the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that restrain blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to purr. And when the bleeding is restrained, then return to your work, as long as you accomplish it; then check with your index finger if there are any small pimples remaining, so cut them and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the pimple, it is not necessary that you cut that pimple at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole pimple, then it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and stitch them now, then when there are no more superfluities for the size of the pimple. It is necessary that you intend to cut the root of it, and drain out pus, and stitch it as we have said. Those pimples that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears better; and pierce it thus as the one before mentioned, in dependence, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment promoting flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	Of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinance, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help them with this because all the veins and arteries of the patient are hot at those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the perdition that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four, a small slit across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the sphygmomanometer, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those parts are comparable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to all of the opening, then splits the keel as far as it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel that flows from where it is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is past because one doubts the strangulation, assemble the .ij. lips of the wound of the heart, and sew all alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this juice until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient is judged to be dead and the lack is in the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut open the epiglottis for those who cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in 3 days or 4.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they command to sew the wound and care for it, until it is healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I see that a young lady took i. a knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by her to cure her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it, and I well know that it had not been cut to a vein nor led anywhere but to the throat, and the veins were passing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I stitched it up, and thus I closed the wound, and I treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it did not happen to the young lady except that she became hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for which I say that in cutting into the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These abscesses are called "goiter hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a bruise, and it is much in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; where natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, where one is similar to fat us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and he has fear, and it is not proper to operate with force except in the one that is small, and he probes and searches all the intromitter.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as our fat, and cannot at any vein, if you cut it, like we cut the ours, and the tract to its whole edge, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and encircle well everything, and cure it as is proper, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways there are to us, of which I will say all the appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and or it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and others.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that others is sometimes and fever-holding, as long as the boils are passed, and is completed the corruption; therefore rests the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the others there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains one abscess, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a pimple, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two appearances, or dry, or moist, and very colored as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument which is called "intropositor," according to its form or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the inquiry of abscesses is that you prick or the moistest part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the intropositor, and take care in those that jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever its color, treat it as I have said of other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the opening moisture comes again, know that it is fat, so treat it crosswise, and take it with pincers, and gently scrape each side and ward off the coat where it lies that you may draw it healthy with the new;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it healthy, then drain it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it remains a little, and the wound grieves you, so apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and restrain the wound, and put on top soothing things for an abscess hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, so cut the two lips of the wound, and cure it with those who cause flesh to grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein pulsating is against you or otherwise hurry and apply the place of pulverized vitriol, and let it lie for two days or three, until the wound festers, and repose the boiling of blood; then return to copper what is remaining of the out.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the intromittent instruments, and there are three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three manners: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine iron, or silver, and the most valuable are those that are yellow, and are more proven to be black pitch for encircling the borders of fistulas;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and so to probes that have two borders in three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and so to probes that have three borders, and are also in three ways; and so to probes that have two borders, and probes of one border only, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these [tools] is made to cut, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, which we use to remove the veins, for this reason one does not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these instruments are the probes put back in handles, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one should only use them in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes i.e. another instrument small, resembling a fist's splints, according to this form, for which one drains blood
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals with incision of veins, and arteries, and sometimes re-enters according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like the breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain misshapen and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to be according to this form of this line from b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then join the .ij. lips of the wound with suture, and treat until it is healed
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the mammary gland is inclined downwards and is softened because of its size as it happens to women, then make a cut in .ij. ribs above, with .ij. similar incisions
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said of suture and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the loss of blood, it is necessary that you fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it absorbs the remaining and grease, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are types of hard scrofulous ulcers or boils and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those who contain moisture it is necessary that they be cut according to this form, from the line b. up to the line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment following this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to boils, then treat it as we have said for incisions of boils, and if the wound returns with pus, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin that is above is joined together, it often comes to abscesses, and this also happens to the vein inflamed and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the one who knows about it then knows as well concerning the artery, then the abscesses are long and they are caused by it.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at your hands, that is to say, it is strangeness; and when it is concerning the vein, then it appears red fire beyond all else.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the armpits and at the groin and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron treatment, and in that which is at the head it is necessary to avoid it also, and in that which is swollen of artery felt from above the skin long;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then operate on the waist as quickly as possible, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle under it, and make it pierce until the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in two lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point the place which is between the two ties with an intromittent as long as the blood issuing from it ceases, and let the abscess be ligated;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the cure that engenders a bow, as long as the ligament holds.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those who have ointment coming after them, as long as it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it is necessary that you grab with your hand those who can bring the abscess to all the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then push the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and let it pierce, and there be i. (one) double thread, so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or tie it from one of two parts with two threads of wool.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, reinsert another needle through all one thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the superfluities exit, then cut away the superfluity from the kernel and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place on one cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer him treatment of poultices and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these happen more often in the shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints, and this is a very painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when one presses it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not at all in the front of the body, but below the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And keep it still from all sides, and do not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go into contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is at the head or forehead, makes the skin to the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then take it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then draw it with the incision, and scrape it, then bone it, and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Never happen in bellies and nowhere else they are called “fungus” because of the appearance of mushrooms, and is the root subtle, and the head large; and there are some small and very large.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one man who had two in his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they were slightly split, and pus came out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 ounces, and the work done in incision is that you look at whether the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and has a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the cut at the spatula is wide, and the fire cautery be in your presence. Because at the cutting comes many times too great a flow of blood, and if without you it goes then hasten thus to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient fearful and afraid of the incision of iron, then take one thread of wool well made, and tie it to the articulation as we have said, and let it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	And then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the thread of wool until he heals the articulation, and feel through it without work; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut even the belly itself, but you may well cut half
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the thread which is of fox color and poor in sense and milk regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a boil, inflamed, and I shall come to its treatment later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the blister has become full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the blister comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the skin, and it is on the belly and there are none of the blisters as there are in other wounds, or of blood which bursts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is by the rupture of the skin and the emergence of the blister, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its ends it rises, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and enlarged much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, nor do you constrain it; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and are filled according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is for windiness, it is puffed up when touched, and the works are that you look whether its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	So it is necessary that you leave the care. Because there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in this chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the belly, it is necessary that you command the patient to hold his arm and be stretched straight, then feel around all around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to breathe deeply between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have felt with the whole palm of your hand,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then the half of the abscess above is to all great one-inch.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot be doubled.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work the half of the abscess extended upon the thread, and put your index finger in it, and seek the interior.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the thread, untie it, and bring the intestine to the outside of the belly.
