et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, then take it with the  cutting tool, and cut away the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery opposes you or the vein, then go well around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a crosswise fashion so that you make it pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then pull the abscess up four fingers above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave them there as long as it should rot, and let the dead flesh drop out by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is delicate and rotten, then cure it as it should be, and cover the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And remove the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it is necessary, and bind the place.
dou chancre	Of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of an ulcer, and how one must work on it by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that the ulcer is generated in the marshes, and great caution should be exercised in its cure, and the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where one can scrape it away like a chancre that is in the armpits, and in the groin, and similar places, and it must all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, then it does not behoove you to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then let him bleed if there is manifest repletion, then make the patient's  good place to perform the work; then throw your curette or ulcer, and shave it on all sides, and ossify it on all sides without leaving anything; and allow the blood to flow out completely, and press well on the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein is against you, then cauterize it as long as the blood is extinguished; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; so it is only lites; and one must not touch with iron in these two likenesses: namely, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy called “litres” with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as coughs and solution of the belly and similar things; if you do not touch with iron because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	lift the patient upright with your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spathule espinous according to this form: And be trenchant of two parts. at the point, and nonetheless be not so entering that it can come just to the intestine when one inserts it, and you cannot pierce it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is situated towards the intestines: then it behoves that you split below the belly .iii. fingers' breadth above the nipple; and if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then let the incision be on the left side of the belly .iii. fingers' breadth; and if it is due to the spleen, then on the right, and it behoves not that the patient lie upon the incision that the superfluities may not run to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it, and raise your hand to the spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as when scraping at the quantity of a fingernail or in equal; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the place eight, and that is the place of the water, then the straw for, and put this instrument from this, here is the form: And it seems like a fine silver dog, and it is made of light iron or archaut, and on the bottom part .i. small hole; and it has on one side, .iii. holes; and .ij. on the other side, and .i. on the other; and the head is cut as much as a feather, and that is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than it behoves in this hour, perchance the patient will die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but in void according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to those that the dispositions of the virtue of the sick signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is retained now by the heart which stops the passage which is on the syfac, because I have spoken of this, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin again the instrument another day, if you see the sick suffering those, and treat of the liquid a small quantity
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this none day, and keep yourself from following until there remains but a little of liquid. And if you doubt about the sick person, and you let him much liquid, so cure him with burial or hot sand, and with much sweat or bath and in the sun, and he is dyed; and cure him with medicines drying until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the liquid, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	At no time are born children who have no holes in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. If this happens as soon as he cannot feel all .i. spatula very subtle according to this form: then put on the hole .i. clo subtle of planc, and tie it and hold it so .iij. days or iiij. And when he wants to make urine, let it be removed the clos, and make urine, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes forward does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is small, if they are medicated with the clo of planc, as we have said, it will widen. Those who do not have the hole in their place are pale, because none are born who have the hole at the head of the penis, which is why they cannot urinate before unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, and the head of the penis and the scrotum are extended as long as a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should; and keep watch for blood loss which often comes, and if it happens, let the stanch who stanches blood do so, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blemishes come on the penis, and is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it is necessary that you prick them with i. one fine needle, and scrape and clean all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blemish is malignant, of putrid color and odor, so it is necessary that you bring cautery to it. When you have scraped it, and if the blemish is in the bottom of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the blemish which is inside first; and when it is healed, then cure the outside. For when you cure it all together, it is not certain that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come in its penis and in the groin; so it is necessary to shave off all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour which is made of the bark of pomegranate trees and vetiver, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if the discharge of blood comes, then administer the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauteries are helpful for two types of situations together: that is, for the discharge of blood and for corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, it is necessary that you put or lead a cane of wood into the penis, and urinate the patient amongst; and when the skin becomes irritated at the tip of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is an ulcer or abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with one sharp instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	and if it is a grievous thing to consider these, so it behooves you to scar them that is to say with a spatula any point of the top of the member and of the skin; then separate well between two, and put one subtle drape of linen moistened in cold water, that it does not dry up.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not of the healing kind like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will and properly on children, it becomes necessary that we do the best work, and the easiest to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have more than what we acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I wanted the most part of the masters and surgeons who did circumcisions near .i. dal, and as forces, and with a whole novacule; so fuioit the keurs because there are .ij. cloths, and perhaps if one cuts the above and leaves the below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is convenient to cut, and the pain is doubled, and to the purification which is due dal it is not assured the point of the member; and to the purification of the angle perhaps the iron escapes, and runs the work, and many times they are born as if they do not need purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done with force to all the line of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, so equally in one all soul tightens; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not force him only to tie the thread around the phallus just so, and then let him enjoy in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then let him be held straight between your hands, and place the force between your hands or below your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the phallus and blow where the heart is, and pull it upwards until the head of the phallus is in. Then cleanse well the filth that is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie below one pock to another link; and hold it as two fingers by the second link to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the two links, then lift the heart upwards gently and pull the head of the phallus.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let it clot blood a pock and pock, for that is the way to heal; and put powder on top and on top of the powder one drapelet glued with an omelet of cooked egg tempered with rose water, confited with good rosy oil and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the fortification is this: the two shoulders be held and be sharp, and the shoulders also as big as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the fortification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it behooves you to extend it to your finger, so that the lesions make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then take pliers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce .iij. days, and that which is below the shaft is swollen, leave it until the abscess heals, and gently scrape it; then cut it as much as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will do it no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound with powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut beyond measure the kernel, and it goes upwards, it will do no harm; cure therefore it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from an obstacle in the bladder, or from blood clotted, or from a bowel, or from flesh thickened, or from similar things that we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not discharged, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and therefore the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, for which reason the urine is discharged.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer an extraction to all the instrument which is called «siringue», of which this is the form: and let it be a fine silver one, light and feathered, like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be a palm length and a half long, and let it be fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie to the chief one pock of wool or cotton, and put the chief of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it until the chief of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit upon one seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and oil of olive and tepid water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently put the syringe in the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis from above towards the bud; then put the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient coming until the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless for that the conductor or where it goes is twisted; then is the thread all the wool pock and pock, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and recommence the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient be aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood comes in the bladder, or there is assembled rotting, and you see it distilling sharp waters and medicines, so do to all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and that is the form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has .iij. openings: .ij. on one side, and .i. on the other, as you see; and its lips are shaped so that the medicine sits such that it stops the penis well without addition, so that if one can draw the moisture out, and pour out when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you want to put your medicines in the bladder, put the chief [part] of the  "keusteur" into the moisture, and draw with the drawing tube which is within it; so that you will draw the moisture into the "keusteur", and then firmly reinsert the inner tube; so that the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the clyster which is used to irrigate the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or lead, and the head is higher; and below .i. finger or where the armpit falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you want to irrigate the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed by a double good thread, and heat .i. pot of that moisture over the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the vagina, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture coming, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make .i. circle, and pierce it roundly throughout; then put .i. strong thread in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles .i. dial, and put inside that which you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work of size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you it openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hareng, and hardens the patient's penis, and he can many times, and then urinates; and with many of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they have 4 years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is as the middle for those who are between childhood and old age; and the cure is lighter from those who have the large stone, than from those who have the small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the mucus that is in the intestines. Because it sometimes hinders the seeking of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and pull them and move them downward so that the stones descend to the front of the bladder, and at no time leave their high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is all declining down; then the cheek and touch it from within.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut above the stone. And if it does not fall to the touch of all, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an accomplished young man; and put it in its base, and touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, move it to the neck of the bladder; then press upward with your finger, and put it outward where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where one makes the incision; then put the spatula cutting, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between that which is between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight on the stone, and your two sides are either foundation or bottom, and be the waist double-traversed so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if the two sides which are foundation or bottom, that it leaps forward without work; and know that there is such stone which has angles, and edges: so is it hard to insert; and if it is such which is below, seeming like a gland, and rounded, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To this one therefore where it has angles and edges, make the waist larger; and if it does not jump forward, then it is necessary that you pull up with tongs which are also like a file at the head, so that moving  you can restrain the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below the .i. instrument subtle curved at the head; and if you cannot engineer it thus, then enlarge .i. pock the opening, and if its sans decorts, then restrain with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there are more than one stone, first put the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then push the tract, and the small ones after if there are more. And if it is very large, it should be soired, and make a bigger wound. Because two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through where the leak cannot close; but nevertheless, you try to drain it, or to break it with tongs, until you pull it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have finished your work, smear the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it steady, and put a soft cloth on top in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck, and do not loosen the tie until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, moisten the place well with oil and water, then treat it with diaphania ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corrosions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and by this urine is held back, which is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore thou shouldst put in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then raise the wound of sharp and smooth and soft, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs, and gather the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the penis is conducted, and fixed within, and the urine cannot issue; so cure of this that I say also, that you cut it many times, it is excused from the cutting by this cure. I have already proven this so.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this form and have it made with three angles on one stick:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the stick into the shaft lightly until it reaches the stone; and turn the stick in your hand at the stone, poke and poke, until you can feel the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. Soon it is broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then make the shaft straight with the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the threads, and cleanse the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the women’s stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, it is the grief of cure, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well knowing who exposes herself to the mires, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, therefore it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well knowing, and at pains find one, and if you do not find one, then do not ask for a virgin chaste midwife; and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then it befits her to push her groin or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she forces it below her groin, and she recommends that she push her groin or cone with the sick person, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder formed.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it befits her to move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the cone, where it is seen appearing, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her groin above the stone or below, and let the waist be at first small;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then push the root in the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as long as the stone can possibly issue forth, and know that many ways of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and soft, long and rounded, and which have reins. Know these resemblances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the stone pains him, put ground vitriol on it and hold it there for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is weak, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone pains him, and it is from the artery that is cut, put powder on the place and restrain it with bandages and splints, and do not restart those again, and leave the stone and do not remove it, except perhaps the patient will die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the tissues are healed, then return to your work as long as the stone is weak.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else than a gathering of moisture or white syfac, which is the substance under the shell of eggs, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and sometimes is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the egg between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have any other part.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes from the eggs, and is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the eggs, and this moisture has many colors: either it is declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is or white like we have said, then the abscess is ripe, i.e., long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the pores, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper skin, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the pores and the white like that, one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you should probe with the whole introducer (tool), from which its shape was described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of this which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his strength and the filling of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him much of cloth;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the sides;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula lead, and cut the skin of the sides among them, from long to near the armpit, and let your cut be straight by dividing the skin of the sides up to the white syfac, and gently scrape it according to your strength;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the syphus with clear water one [large] opening, and extract all the water, and then put your bandages, and keep the syphus above; and do not touch the heart of the stones, but only the syphus; cut out all or by pieces evenly the costal part of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the sheaf falls to your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the syphus; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the stones with a suture, and then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the sheaf corrupted by another illness, then it befits that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the discharge of blood; then cut the stone to all the suspender, and extract the sheaf, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the liquid is assembled into two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound a linen cloth moistened in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put another linen cloth moistened in wine and oil, and place the two pads on top, and put doubled cloths on top, and tie it above all the linen according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths and use them like woolen padding according to this appearance and be assembled by stitching at the waist of the breeches, and one of the arms reaches onto the foundation up to the back, and the other to the armpit; and the other part goes above the two shoulders, and all of it is assembled together in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this ramice of cautery is medicined in the place of iron size, and it is that you prick i. a subtle cautery cultellaire, and cut the skin of the genitals, and be scorched as we have said, so that the white syfac containing the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cut in all ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and move guarding against bleeding, and moves than the works of iron;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing opposes you, or abscesses or discharge of blood or other things, so treat what opposes you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer the puncture as I told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs that we have said that the watery root is there,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below to the full spatula width, and put the puncture deep into the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the water flows out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave for the remaining water to flow out, then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not let the water issue from the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put in it a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrops, for its form is before; and enlarge i. pock the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or until when it becomes, and when it is assembled as before, and thus will pass the patient his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this vein there is fear in more positions, for which it seems to me that one better leaves it;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the joints; and this is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excess of sour and acrid matter, which is spread to the joints, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and does not find any pain, and is a grave abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance there are some abscesses fearsome and hard, and of a reddish color, and at times comes from a vein or an inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by a vein, then it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not advisable that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	The one which is caused by an inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition at the expression of the touch of the fingers,
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well do surgery on this kind, and on the other wounds;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then the leaf is on top, and the root from white side, and deliver the suspension from all sides of the leaf.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the leaf is already boiled with these new wounds, then it is necessary that you draw out the leaf, and cut it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the air, or in those that are inside the vessels, then you must deliver all of that vein, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is or its rear, then it behooves you to cut it completely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cover it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed in a covering resembling that of one testicle, with the softening of the testicles,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves greatly when he goes.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	And the cure of this malady is as carefully prescribed as the preceding one.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And nonetheless, we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on one level seat, then put the suspensory of the loincloth down to his two [legs].
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	To all the vessels which are near to the penis, and the masters braid them, and they extend;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then cut with a sharp spatula wide through the vessels, until they are exposed.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	And then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert an awl where there is one thread double, and tie it at the first place where the vein came, and tie it straight to the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then the head is placed directly in the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound like the others where one avoids a boil, so that no vessel bursts that would nourish one of the corners.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by these there comes no harm, and to all the vessels comes life, so it is necessary to draw out the corners of all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the flesh does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sinew
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The happenings of this branch are because of the section that comes to or from the sinew, or the stretching over the belly in the part of the ribs, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either of the sinew or from the stretching of it, and these two manners of much come from causes: whether by percussion, or jumping, or wrestling, or lifting of heavy loads, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it's of the stretching of the sinew, are that they have pain and pain, in long lengths, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and is the abscess even up to the base, because the pus quickly follows the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the pus, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscess is various appearances, under the skin near, and this because of the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the pus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it descends the edges with the pus, and is held in, and causes great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, so it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to return the intestine into its place in the wound, if it can enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either support it on his neck between your hands, and raise his hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles down to their length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push into the folds of the waist tweezers according to what you need to open the wound, and make it such that the entrails can issue forth.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the skin that is below the skin of the groin, until the white skin underneath is uncovered on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then put your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white skin that is below the skin of the buttock, and between the second skin;
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and depart that which is behind the buttock, and between the second skin; and then move with your right hand into the center of the groin, and have the white skin on top in your left hand, and lift the buttock all over the skin towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the minister that he extends the buttock upward, and undoes that which is above behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and if it has a point of the intestine enveloped or white hard thing, and if you find any such thing, send it to the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or it has one thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, which we have said is below the skin of the groin, with a strong ligature of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then envelop the hairs of the threads, and tie them together forming two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter in, except that an abscess may come.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the thread directly according to the first thread long two fingers of that one, and after those two threads leave the suture which is below the heart of the cords the length of a finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the cords, as long as the sinew, and the bone, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it in the wounds, and place the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And no time is cauterized the white suture that we have said, after the incision, out of fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and let the linen be as long as it drips through; and if it delays in dripping, then be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it drips.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this treatise I never saw anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like the branch which is assembled with the vein, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or slightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who operate, as long as the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the bowels, as we have said, and opens them; and do not separate any of the intestines from the joints, and if any are separated, it is little, and repair all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nonetheless if it stays too long in this position, the wound or ulcer grows, as long as the intestine is separated;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the extension of the soft part which is in the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen its limbs and opened;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure of this is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies commonly on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated with a width according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the soft part which is under the skin that follows it, then take the iron and put it over the place appearing of the soft part;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press at the front of the belly, then count the two apparent eyes of the sifac upon the head of the thigh, and count one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the thigh, and do not cut the sifac nor extend any other thing, as I have made you know in the cure of the root of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then cure by the cure of wounds. And when you cut the filaments, then make it clean and cure the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sifac is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles softens in some men, because the sacs that are inside are softened, and it is made visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and one cuts the skin that is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three sutures or four firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that chastisement is common in our law, and for this reason I would like that I do not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two manners: one is that the mules know how to respond when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often have need of chastisement of some beasts to help us, as of goats and sheep and calves and other beasts. I say therefore that chastisement is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by flaying. In the one which we do by attraction, we make our sit the beast in hot water, until the testicles are softened and pendant; then taking them with your hand, as long as they are put back and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is according to two manners as men: one if between the two sexes appears as the figure of nature of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. And the other manner is in women, and has on the groin as a penis and two sexes. And the cure of the man and of the woman is that you cut the hairs attached all, and cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.
