Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a hair attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that's the cure. It behooves you to pluck the excess of the tenting with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and don’t pull too much so that bleeding doesn’t come out, then the cure of other cures until it is healed; and at another hair that is born at the mouth of the privy parts, and the employment, and by chance jumps out, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this reason they called it the ancients "cow disease". If it behooves you to cut it, as we have said the tenting, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of erratic if is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accident by illness that has come to it; or it is by the joint being joined together, or by subtle or thick mucus, and it is made in the ribs, or in the sides, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and by adventure the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the gaze of the female. If the obstruction is near appearing, if you wish to do it with your two fingers or to the belly. If it is subtle mucus, and it is near the two leaves, then haste, and let it be this way: put your two fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then when the two leaves are formed, as long as the subtle mucus is round, and the obstruction is over; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and lay the woman down at home each day, so that it cannot heal. And if the mucus is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a spatula resembling the leaf of myrtle. If the obstruction is of flesh born, then suspend it to the loincloth and cut it; and have medicines that stop blood, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, together with an abundance of egg white; then administer a cane of broad plantain, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus be long, and administer a tent of dry linen; then cure them with other cures until it is healed. And when in the ribs comes flesh born, then it should be cut according to this manner, if it is not abscesses festering. Because at the festering abscess that is in the ribs, one must not touch to do.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without court accustomed use, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thick; and we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that resolve healing. I say that hemorrhoids and the thick, when they are made in the buttocks, and they do not appear to the touch, unless the cure with iron. Those who are at the mouth of the buttocks, one can feel them, are those that one can cure. So it is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then the thick as tongs, and the cope at their roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the air for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if it decorates of blood comes, so let her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and galangal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and bind it with honey and aisil, and make .i. plaster on her back. And if it hardens, that is good. If not, then let her put leeches to the back and nipples without iron; then take flax, and soak it in plantain juice or in elderberry juice with old wine, and make it lay there.  And when the abscess rests, cure its place of ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and is similar to .i. hard head, so it must be covered as I said the thick; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the buttocks
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the buttocks, such as chancre and purulent abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more diseases that I have said in the division. So it is necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the buttocks, which is not of abscesses that boil over; and if you want to know the work of iron, look at whether the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.  Therefore do not haste to pierce, but let it die until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have .ij. small stools where he leans, and support his back and assemble his feet to the sides of the leg; and let his hips be spread out, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good linen; then suck him down towards the right side, and administer the instrument that is used to open the mouth of the buttocks, so that after comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see to administer this instrument, you first put the tip in order to know the depth of the buttocks, so that what enters into the instrument does not go further than it should, and that it does not blister the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the buttocks with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and one holds it in his hand soft, it must be covered at the top, at the spathe leaf; and when the boil is emptied, it is necessary to put in the wound tents soaked in rose oil, or in green oil; and put the tent further from the wound to the bottom of the buttocks, and put outside on the buttocks and on the linen pad soaked in water or malves are cooked; then cure after .ij. days of ointment before this, until it is healed; and some time lift the buttocks and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and long arcturus that have been cooked; then return to the ointment. And if the wound is returned in the buttocks, it is necessary that you guard yourself from ironing, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air: then the child hastens to issue forth; then you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the head first, and the second with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the child comes out soon; for when it ascends onto its head, then the second follows with it, and the world is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it comes sometimes on its feet, and comes forth from the body or the shoulder, or the hands, or it comes on its belly, or on its back, and is converted by chance onto its neck, and by other bad figures; it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural issue, and the woman giving birth cries loudly, and the virtues of her are weak, then make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and arose her nature d’oile or fenugreic be cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula whose shape is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cuts the secondine and clips at its nail until the moisture which is inside comes out; and presses the woman's belly as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fenugreek mulch with sesame oil; then make her breathe and sneeze with condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child will now be born. And if the two hands come out far, then it is necessary that you gently pull them back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on one seat, and lift her feet up; then overturn the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the overturn; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the knife which is before put, and extract the child, and reset it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, then it is necessary to push upwards.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn it back and forth, until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then pinch one of the parts and extend it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	It cannot jump as far as the hips, if it is commanded to jump, and make it sneeze from condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then turn it back and forth until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For therefore it is easily remedied.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not heal as we have said, then take a sprig of alder, and oil of sesame, and melted wax, and grind all in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put upon the woman's nature inside and outside this ointment.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have him sit upright, leaning until beneath the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened underneath, have him placed i.e., a collar of myrrh, and place it underneath, and let him leave it for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have him sit on i. seat, then have him sneeze and restrain his mouth and nose, and take hold of his belly lightly, for the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then the midwife puts her hands here and there.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then either she supports him on his neck, and lets the feet hang down, and either he lies on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and she bends her hands here and there, and then she takes the hands above his belly, and she moves the cushions underneath, so far as she is prepared below.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then she takes his feet and moves them forcefully, then she moves his belly upward, and then she puts her hands in;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and rock the child back and forth; and command the woman to remain still until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child coming out with one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to devise bringing back the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then have the woman lie down and go away;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, put her on a bed, i.e., lying down, and prop up her legs;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the liniment that I have recounted;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, put her on a stool, then study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and expel the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and command her to strain until the infant emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned toward the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the midwife hold his hand then turn it a little bit, and the elbow gently.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is aligned, put it on the muscled natural height and oil, as we have said, then command her that she move it a little bit.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on one seat, and command her that she strain herself; and then let her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all of the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to doing in this way to all the spine, so seize the spine at your finger, as long as the moisture is emptied
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can't bear on its face and on its neck, then grasp from the shoulder, so that it doesn't be held back, and let the child die
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to not  get pregnant again
adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore, if it is gently straightened.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live, if they can be named;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiplied, and are devised by the syfaci who divides them, which is linked to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they arise as naturally as ones all under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they arise grievously, then the cure is as we have said, and let the bailiff be subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it pertains to salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Never are formed in the marshes i.e. one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its wise glory,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all these things, because perchance similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so be done according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman who has a dead child in her womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or she has fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if it is necessary that the woman be supported on her back, and her hips are inclined downwards, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister takes the plait of two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it is not moved by the descent of the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare's with moist oils with a poultice of alum and fennel and flaxseed, then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and these poultices.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then put them in the mare lightly, then choose one place where she puts her hind legs that are suitable for this.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take ward if the child is appearing that it descends on its head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he places the pins in his eyes or neck or mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the groin or near the ribs
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on the feet, he places it or pricks it and the middle ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the pin in his right hand, and puts the curve between his two fingers of the left hand, and pushes it gently with all his hand, and places the pin in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then set against one other bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions be equal
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then set them equally by moving from one side and the other, so that they move smoothly, and let the bones be toothed so that they hold together, as in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then take some of his oil and put it in that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if none remain, then put this bone or higher up its place, and do this until it all comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes forward of the other, and it cannot be brought back by constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then it behooves you to wrap around it that is, a bandage, until it heals entirely;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then the bandage in the joint of the foot or to the knife, and thus it behooves you to do in the other hand, and two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is protruding in its exit, or it has a sharp top assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two, and make the chief and extract the water.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	Or you take it with the instrument that is called "almidach," because the form comes with the instruments or chapter that is after this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And in the same way, do it if the child has a large head naturally.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	Then pull apart the bones with pliers.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the head leaps out and is forced back, it may be split, as long as the moisture which is or worse has issued forth.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if it cannot issue forth, cut it into pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, it behooves you to pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the application to the mouth of the mare is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is strained in the belly or chest, then it behooves you to extract it, that is, envelope it with a cloth wrapped on the hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make the belly or chest compress as long as the moisture there is corrected;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are set and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then force the bailiff to thrust his hand into the cavity of the joint, and draw it up to the mouth of the joint;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then he puts one or two, and the wood is cured.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the abscess is constricted by hot cauteries which have come there, one should not work on it.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	otherwise, one should administer moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administer plasters, and soak in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, so administer what we have said in a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do this, then the thigh shall be treated by parts, and nothing of the second part shall be left behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if it comes to an abscess in the groin, administer what we have said about poultices.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if bleeding occurs, then apply a cold compress and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time there came an abscess in the belly, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to drain profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered for a long time, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because this one whose belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I examined the wound, and in my hands bones, as long as the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I visited the woman long time thus, and it grew to be a small piece of belly from there;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter for those that, when masters find a strange thing, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the presser, which we have in the books; and at two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the staff be 1. i. two palms wide, and the margin of the trees i. must, and long one palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and among the two limbs be adjusted by this same staff, which be firm in one and in the other, half palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the furrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, in its semblance more subtle and lighter, be made of ebony or boxwood staff, according to the likeness of tongs;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have as two shoulders two attachments, as you see, of one palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the womb with all the instruments, make the woman sit on one bed, feet apart and legs open;
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two attachments together in the womb, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with the instrument, as you have done with the pliers evenly, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the womb, until the patient does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all mounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the viewer has seen them appeared, so much is more haste the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If it does not despise the instrument that you do not have it appeared, because their necessities is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, it behoves that you command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze from condiment, and hold her hands to the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she leaps for this, well is it.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not happen, take one pot and make a hole or cover it, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or none of them, be cooked or put in water over the fire; then put a band or hole in the pot and the other end in the mouth of the marsh
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and steam it until the vapor comes from within the marsh; then let her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second time he sneezes quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more force, command the lady to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in musk of Altai, and then put it in the vagina.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And seek the second one; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the root does not fall out during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	But it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes out and dislodges itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the root is narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not of all those we have said, so guard that you do not use on milk.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the uterus, you tie it to the hip bone of the woman, then the enema with ointment tetra-pharmacon.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she will bear it and put it back, and will come forward; but nonetheless, when she bears it so comes a bad smell to the stomach and head, and pales the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument for fumigating the woman at the time of childbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is shaped like a cage, and one places the fine tip in the body, and the limbs wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be on the coals, and the tinder as long as it is burning, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but it is stifled by subtle artifice.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it behooves the midwife that she pierce that artifice to its due, and do not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and guard the opening so that she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place upon it half a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then the ointment's cure until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, then place upon it a piece of plank and leave it for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And at times this stoppage comes from a scab of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that scab; if cured, as we have said of the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules, and larger than those that come from beside the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it works, and still moisture mixes with white or subtle pus.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are passed; and they are known by those who have them or by excretion or flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps one jumps towards.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and reach to the junction of the hip, and to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing to the base, and not piercing:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your thumb or foundation, and insert a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is crookedness, then put a tent of fine lead, or one hair of a horse, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it and there is no emission through the opening or windiness or liquid, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	Know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced to the bladder or to the urinary passage, if it leaks urine, and cannot be closed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes up to its place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the pain is within the area, then it is that it is bowed in there, and there is no worth of medicine nor healing by ointment;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistula openings there is no cure but labor, and vanity of the foolish remedies that intervene in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those which are not pierced nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you raise his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert an awl of iron, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the awl comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the base, then you must put your index finger there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and feel then that the awl has pierced it; and whether discovered or not you feel between your finger the bone or flesh, then you know that it is passed;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work with it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says nevertheless that one can well heal none, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid one makes it, if one carefully heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and it is pushed completely hot into the fistula, until it reaches the base; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these char-like fibers are burned, which resemble an owl's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of tents moistened in butter, as long as that char is healed, then the cure of ointment tightening flesh and welding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, well. Otherwise, it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent gets in and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your bottom and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or silk, and you see the fistula according to what follows the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then cauterize after, as long as it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and will be delivered the tent, and it will shrink; then cut those parts that seem a feather of an owl, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the skin pulls out, and goes between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cautery of fire joins two good things: namely, the burning of those joined parts, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then cure with tents soaked in butter or ground herbs, until the wound lies low, and the burned parts are inside the bottom;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then cure the wound of the eyes by putting on a hard dried bandage, and those are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way down to the bottom and is separated from the body, you put your hand or foundation there and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tendon and between two or the skin or sheath where it is close to piercing, then there is only a way of hope and assurance, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put tents and dress it like the first
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not let them go too deep, that you do not cut into the tissue that holds the base, and let the secretions come out by their own will
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then dress it, as we have said
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound after it is cut to its base, or by tent or other pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then mend the flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound, and leave the fistula in the part outside the foundation; so it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are this way: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or costs near the foundation next to the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	If you take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one twisted thread into two, and puts the tent on all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is inserted into the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread from that which was pierced, just as you put your finger or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two ends together, and bind them to each other, and leave it for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no time, as long as the threads close those gaps that are between them, and stick together;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make by the lacing cover if too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula spine from which one makes the fistula is very useful, on one part and trenching;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because of this one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to two ways: or they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short they bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and furthermore adds or a drop of citrine water or a drop of blood, and have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, if it is that you command the patient to stretch so that they go into chambers, as long as the foundations are sore and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and can take it with pliers, or hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the forceps cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with one drapery, or cotton, or a piece of felt;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and the you pull them to your two, then cut them, and powder above some hot powders that are in place of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot issue, then enema the patient with a harsh and biting enema to wash what is in the foundation so that it can issue openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient feels no pain, and if the threads are far from the foundation, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is that you prick them with your finger or pliers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until it is healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is fitting that you administer the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	And if it be too wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do likewise with all others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation one layer of soft cloth in rose oil or in cerote, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until they itch, and when they are healed, treat them with ointments and other remedies until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Dryness of the bowels or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times dryness of the bowels occurs in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then it is necessary that you scrape to the point of a spatula or your fingernail the bark above, which does not let it get moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then cure until it is healed as it should;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure until it is healed.
dou fremit	Of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formic is a small appearance false near the body, and goes much into it.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it is found cold, and one feels it as much as dead from chill, and comes in the whole body, and more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of an goose feather, or a feather of a strong vulture, and put that cane on the chill, until the circles purple the chill all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand to the whole cane until you cover all around the chill, and put it in deep, and scrape the chill from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do this of a dog of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, for the two to hold, and move pressed And if you see, so cauterize the frenulum, as it is before or in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At no time is made a clister of silver or wood, or iron melted or woven; and at no time is made of these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are administered in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is inside pierced; and has on one side two pierced, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly is where one puts medicines from a bladder of beast or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each opening one must have space, then put into these openings one strong thread of flax twisted in ten or as much as it enters, and assemble the belly as if it were a sheep's.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then tie it with a strong thread in front of the instrument, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then squeeze the minister with his two hands together, until it is all emptied, then extract the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the side.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to work well, let it itch as much as possible; and if it burns one whole night, it is more effective help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema the patient with illness of stomach pain, and the medicine works quickly, then repeat it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base or an abscess, then the enema should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And this is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or with spear or staff or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head, simple ones, because remembrance comes in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt greatly of a hot abscess: if the one does come forth soon from the head itself even if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the blood on the contrary side of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient from eating wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be less, and drink no wine, nor eat any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, a cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in styptic wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the artist has moved it, put some ointments on it, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with tents, then assemble them with stitches, as I will say for belly wounds, of stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a bit, then cut it away; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked barley, also chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, so cut away the rottenness all, and throw out the pus, then cure it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which does not close on its own, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then you must stop the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which binds as soon as the wound has closed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	And apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place until it dries well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And then cover it well, and leave it unbandaged unless it swells; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime when one has neither incense nor dragon’s blood, but that the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has healed the wound, even when it is still there, do not put on this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But put on some digested ointment, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it is swollen;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you after these fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it to heal and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of those is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let it be the medicine soft, such as calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and calcined water also in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other ores of this kind, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it and tie it with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of a swelling, pierce or lower.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and there comes a flow of blood, then staunch it, and bind it, and cauterize it if that is necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is guarded, so that the meat goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the heart on the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural form;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then the strapping happens frequently, and it is left for some days, then it is cured by ointment of drying until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, so it will.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	And if there are pieces of bone, then you must treat the ones that you can reach. And as for those that you cannot reach, leave them until the wound dries up.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And so it will be cleansed and aligned at the exit;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, see if there is air escaping from the wound as the patient breathes; you then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then put no powder to it in the first hour, nor bind it at all for the blood that it does not remain in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the heart, and close up the wound of the sick person;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but put a drawing ointment on it, and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, put in the wound old cotton to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes no spasm, nor evil trembling of heart nor drawing in of the leg;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good arrangements, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal it therefore with bandages and other dressings, until it be healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and work, then you know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, then treat it as before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it is deep in the bone and has broken pieces, clean the wound, and remove the fragments if they are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not loose, let the wound rot, it will lighten the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And judgments of other wounds on other limbs are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The displacement of the belly is great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From the great wound jumps no times the intestine, or the nerve of the intestines, because of which the intrusion of others;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes worse the small wound than the great.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason one puts back the intestines into place, if they are not put back hot on hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they enter no more into place,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason the middle wound is worse, for this reason one resets the intestine to its place just like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is in four ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one each and explain.
