Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine has emerged,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if it seems something should be returned, then it is done by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Dip a sponge or soft cloth in hot water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil it in water with quince and spice.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and apply the intestine as long as the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine restraining is done, and it is moved to release air.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and herbs be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by these it is aligned the entry to little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make an opening in the wound with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to move the waist
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut there except with great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if cut inside in the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine leaps out
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put it back in its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able, because this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and buttocks higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you set your attention to that the sunken part be higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds put that which has appeared to you.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have between your hands one minister pitiful who holds all the fracture to his hand
et assemble les levres;	and assembles the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of sutures,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity and width of the wound
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then let space from the head of the wound one finger's width, and put a needle where it has a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two points of the skin with the two points of the shaft;
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin within, as long as you make it pierced from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two heads of the shaft the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the strain of a double thread around the needle of two parts
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the two heads of the wound evenly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one to two finger widths, and insert another needle there;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread just as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease doing this according to what you need of needles
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	as long as the entire wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles be medium, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the fine needles cut all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they should be shortened
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	that they do not cut and open the wound before the soldering;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then clip the heads of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I place tents or cloths on the shoulder of the needles to keep them tight.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and I let them be until the wound is closed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for one or two needles suffice there.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two heads of skin and the two heads of fascia together with a needle where there is one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced these four heads together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then wind the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews draps;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each seam the thickness of a man's finger.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this seam should be sewn up for the man
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound that one had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was slashed with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	And the wound was more than a palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was two palms wide of the intestines
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine after it had been 24 hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And was the wound sewn for fifteen days, and I treated it, and it became healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in one place where they found none, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and laid half a cloth on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and thrust it from the outer part to the inner one;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the core straight through, then lay the tip of the thread or suture where you have thrust the needle;
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from the inner part to the outer one;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier does furs.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the side of one part, and take it back from the other, as long as the sewing is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of sewing, which Galen says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like any one who brings together the two parts naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they support one head of the bone to the other head, in such manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or head of a trocar near, and make him feel only that side.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the two heads of the bone
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make him feel from the outside part to the inside one
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the two shoulders
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make one and the other feel from the outer part until that inside, in two other shoulders of the miracle that are on the other side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most usual manner of stitching and the most common
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Gauls say this word, and no one testifies
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corded things;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the sewing more serious than the others places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the fire had touched it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then return to sew the intestine and the cut; then put above the powder that is preventing decay
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire had touched it, put above some ointment that is present, until the wound closes;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and stitch the thread, and suture the fascia, and the muscle.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, place on top of it, as soon as it begins to fester, old cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicines in many dispositions as long as the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make community with the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of thyme heated, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the edges, and below the buttocks;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or rot in the bowels, and it happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if he administers black wine enemas, and even if the rot comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called 'young' cannot heal when it is rotted,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	And it is for the placement of the veins that they are, and for the delicacy of the whole body, and the approximation of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back as if it were an intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is old and has turned into a worm or black, then you must tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not come from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligaments
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound until outside to align the extraction when the joint falls and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If it can be restored in some people,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that one man was pierced through the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and formed a fistula, and through it there was discharge and wind.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the bones joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it join, I doubted that the patient would have ill in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no ill, but he remained in better dispositions, and ate and drank.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And said any experimentors that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take fresh sprigs of herbs, then assemble the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	And when the sprig has opened its mouth, place it upon the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth upwards;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then bind its head, and this holds so that it cannot be loosened,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put one other fream afterward in that manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and stitch up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the chief one becomes inflamed in the intestine, and no trouble comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if it is possible to tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine that be very cleaned
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread i. a thread of linen fine twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and wind it back in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of suturing of limbs is not different except according to the way of hope and expectation.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the hollow bowels, there is nothing but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula,"
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and also when it is raised and bent back.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to truth a hard and white knot, in which one feels no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also raised like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it appears clear and bent back, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes a little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or for its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside it, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or when the matter is corrupted, and the substance is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late for digestion, and late for health, and inflated by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary that I make you know the cure of a fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the stomach, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the backbone of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens to the property of the principal limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grave healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it known, then take a tent of iron or of iron, if the fistula is straight, if it is crooked;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then circle it with a subtle tent of lead;
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the lead bends and molds around the tortuosity;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	And if the fistula has been opened by hands and you cannot well search it with probes.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of the openings.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture spreads from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then carefully probe its depth, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and whether it is closed off completely;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well of the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then strike according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the foulness and corrupt flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the cure until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep well in a right place, it is necessary that you cut it as deep as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist tents in sharp medicine and insert them to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments to close the sore flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by those, then cauterize it as we have said
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve strikes your main limbs or principal members as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then cut out as much as the corruption is
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal with things to bring flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and returns crooked like before
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone far enough
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and want as long as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot succeed there;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other thing than to leave to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers;
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you extract it with an instrument suitable for that,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then extract them all, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it copes with moisture and flesh, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put upon the wound something preventing decay,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and therefore they will have lighter bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then remove only the corruption until all blackness is gone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corruption, and it comes to the flesh of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it must be cauterized and covered all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the substances came to the leg, and became swollen with a large abscess, and had no external cause to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the surgeon because of his folly opened it so much that the abscess opened.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and from it flowed out a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came much pus that all stank foul and moist from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a miracle they cured for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those who ran through the courts with great noise;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the body of the youth, and had a citron colour.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I placed a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then hastened, and dug into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was that one who appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for the one that I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicine of boiling water over a long time, and it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I took out the bone, and I was afraid to sew up the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do more than when I came upon one palm of the bone, and the tract was brought to all its length.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with remedies; and he was healed and joined firmly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it no longer became necessary to begin the work except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	Because for blood evacuation it often occurs, but he was healed entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in the place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary to anything at all, neither for walking nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it should be treated in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one linen cloth, and strap it to the head of the bone that is opened
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command that he extend it upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put one other linen band thicker than the first band, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh outward,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh at the place where you wish to operate, so that the pus does not stain the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put one coal or a board under the bone so as to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to be so careful as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be even more so another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if uncover the flesh entirely; then put one coal underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then let it move from one side to the other, and let the string of the corruption be long, i.e., a point, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and let the bone on which it rests be on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is in the heel of the hand or in the heel of the foot, then this thing is very strong;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the instruments and threads for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of the illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument of which you have need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can dislocate from within or from outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with the cures of medicines, and they do not help at all.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes by these of death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and  it blisters after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold throughout the body; so you hasten to cut,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cut it, and do not give him any space to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, then cut it with a knife; and if it passes the knife, then it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no worth of treatment stronger than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and thus do it when the corrosion comes to one point: if it comes in the first joint, then cover after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on a point, then cover the whole point;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, then cover at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister on the lower ligature, and another minister on the other ligature above,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you shall sever the flesh that is between the two ligatures about one spatule width wide, as far as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cover or so, and put on each side one drape of linen, so that the sore does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And may another injury and abscess come to the patient's leg.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes when you work, then cauterize the place thoroughly,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or where you put any powders restraining; then return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to one man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion first came in his heel of the foot, until it encompassed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man felt the corrosion, he raised himself up to cover his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that the corrosion returned him in the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things  rebounding after the purification of the body, and cannot cease the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wished that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want, because I had hope of rebounding the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and fear also if he cuts his hand, that it will not fester,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the virtues of man were weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he set about covering his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have recounted this tale for the purpose that if one needs it, they may do otherwise.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to its fleshy place and remains so long that it makes a great gathering of flesh.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and the flesh jumps out, and it remains there like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is as fine as one thin veil
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not reach down to the bone or the nerve, and such a malady is called 'healthy'
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes to the bone and perfects, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the treatment for this is that you cut all around the skin, and also when it is thin, like a sheet of cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it will not be able to rot from there.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you believe that the skin has hardened, and the corruption is not yet complete.
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thickened with flesh, then treat it with a clyster like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the breasts are large, and the bowel within them is of foul stench,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take thus, and oil, and lead, equally, and put to cook in 1 vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in a clyster the belly, and hold the anus shut;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine rest for two hours, then remove it by pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the chest is calmed and the fear is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at no time are they to be given a clyster of ash water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present and you take ashes from grapevine wood and pour water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then the flow, and in a cloth, as long as you know that the chest is well-cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if he is cleansed with water and honey or where there is a bit of litharge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you cleanse him with honey and mulled wine, for honey has the property to purify and wash,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes the skin dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are assured that the breast is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clyster of those that causes flesh to be born in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you are to prepare a diaphanous plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cauterize it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have said the properties or how to treat ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening in the chest is small and the cannula of the enema cannot enter it
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it with an iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basil ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, so the cloth and leave it only as much where the clyster may enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that lies above is lower, then cover or more below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the bowel is in its proper place, do not allow any flesh to enter;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it is arranged in such a manner that the bow goes to the lowest place that it is
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the bow is perfect, then it does not allow entrapped flesh
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you are not able to cover the breast below as you see.
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it is arranged in such a manner: that the bow goes gently downward, and nothing of the bow remains;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take solidifying medicines to put upon the chest,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and be upon it, that is, a linen cloth covering the whole chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cover with force the opening of the chest, that is, a bit larger than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then put ointment of sulfur upon another cloth according to the quantity of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it over the opening of the chest to align the ribcage, and do not remove the large cloth outside except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And he who is on the opening of the chest, often remove to remove the ribcage,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know those that flows from the ribcage, if it's venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take guard if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	And when your medicine is spread in such a manner and you see the nature that leaps on the wound of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is healed already, and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change one other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast remains bowed undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, so do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health approaches. For there are men whose healing in their wounds is delayed, and some who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if the breast remains undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to heal, and are swollen, apply drying medicines both in substance and in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as for example diaphinite ointment, because it contains a great part of vitriol, and that is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphinite ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and the same thing made honey cooked mixed;
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when inflammation has ended
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and you take mire and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey when it is over the fire
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then you glue it onto a cloth, and place it on the chest, and every time administer an aromatic herb long
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lilies of heaven, which is also like flour from vetiver and wormwood
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or composites: grind them, and make it into powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long and is not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has gone too far, and it makes an impression in the bone, or hard members, or limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the wound of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaritium is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and care is not taken, then one comes to have another abscess nearby.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they rub and push the bone as long as it rubs against the root of the angle, and by chance they rub it all over.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion to the bone, as long as it comes pain pungent, and is the shoulder two large, and is the color  fused.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut away with iron all the superfluity which is remaining from the bone,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the joint presses against the flesh, and it begins to prick, and to bleed,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a rag under the joint that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the bump on top, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put over the remaining flesh medicinal substances hot and corrosive to remove all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and treat it properly, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the two bones corrupt, cut them in one as it has been said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is broken and bruised, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then cut the angle of the spatula sharply by cutting across from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard so that the waist does not come near the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the hand is relieved
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them come out at the base of the joint, where the birth is in no one of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in neither of the two parts does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of one who is fleshy is light, in such manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, that is grievous to cure; so hold you to cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In he who is born or lies at the back of the buttock, it behooves you to first cut the round flesh until the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then set the bone to a suitable thread for this, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The solderings that come to the two assemblies come from birth, or from the welding of a wound, or from the burning of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you solder that soldering, so that the parts return according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, that they do not solder together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	And you put between two pieces of subtle planks until the joints are united, as it is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the joint comes to any of its two with the palm, then strike that solder as it is fitting.
Des vils	Of vile
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large swells full of melancholic superfluities, that come in more than a few members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often happens in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once expurgation of honey, and then the ointment of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is thus in .ij. ways: one is with the cup, and draw forth black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you lift the vein, and draw it entirely outward.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The waist is thus according to this manner:  first rise the leg with hot water very strong, until the large sinew be softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then constrain the leg of the patient from above the hip to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, of a wide size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then elevate and draw forth the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the strength of the patient can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the wound, and command him to poultice it with meats preventing black mold;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the leg is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, then heat it over the fire, and then apply it to the vein long from the armpit to the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the leather against the skin, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it can be seen red and black, and when it enters or gets into the leather, it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the edge underneath, until it is lifted from the leather, and then place it on the skin lightly;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then the cut is made in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then hold the vein at its source, as you have done, and bend it to another incision, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then make another cut where more is needed, then hold the vein, and cut it at the foot of the two fingers
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and hold it up to the second incision; then extract it from incision to incision until it is completely free, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and raise it, then put a needle to all its one strong double thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and the tie and draw it out, and put it below one-half of its length, and turn your hand this way and that until it comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and guard that she does not break, for if she breaks, then one cannot draw it or raise it, and comes to annoyance for the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have it all drawn out, then put upon the place of the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If it is necessary that you cut it tortuously, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut deeply so that it does not cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And is of thick curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape.
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is situated in legs, in warm places where no herbs nor trees grow, and in land that has no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of rot that comes from under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as it comes from inside the body, serpents and worms, lodged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then its color changes, and the vein begins to protrude outward, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder opens up, then it behooves you to wrap around it a piece of plank from 3 and a half to 2 inches (wide), and bind,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and all times that it is painful to the outside (?), then wrap around the plank, and bind.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut a portion of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, then it enters into the flesh, and brings forth abscess and rot there, and bad sickness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore for that reason it is necessary that it be treated carefully, little by little, until the head, and that nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when it is treated is five palms long, or ten;
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a bone came to me once, which was  10 palms long, and when you cut it, it emits 1 ray or hole, and pierces to the bottom
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all of it emerges; and empty the material which is within, and administer to the place medicines preventing putrefaction any day, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at times to this vein main veins, and also when it opens at the joint of the foot, or foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and much blood comes out from there, and from which they jump veins; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "ox's disease", because it often happens to oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well by the movement from limb to limb, as long as it moves under the skin where it goes, and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by rot of some humors, such as those which come to the belly from serpents and worms and ascarids;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its evil nature, because when it travels through the body and goes up to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drained, one can only flee when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so therefore you must bind the place above and below with a strong linen tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above it and the flesh will follow, and if the vein is pierced into the skin and you don't find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire above until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is when it inflames the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or chief near the eye, hold below him the eyebrow form, then cut above, and treat the further.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body of medicinal solutions for the corrupted humid humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if worse of meat causing putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This sickness is called “wakiring” in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	More quickly than anything else, just as living silver when it cuts from its place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that place and settles in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little while after, it spreads throughout the body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it returned to the middle of her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never wished this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had wished many that they well would move pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not wish it so, as I see it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason appears that constraint of windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear so according to this reason to those who are delicious and who have moist bodies and veins full.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if it lies above and below evenly, and then cut above until that constraint of windiness at its place is gone;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you cannot see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of those who bring forth wind, such as foul pills, and pills of serpentaria, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of them is that some have large points, and small, and hairy, and smooth;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some that have two angles, and those that have tongues, and those that have parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that fall in any member, they fall in two ways: either in the principal member it falls,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If it is necessary that you take care of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in many situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps out the sfeacus which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is when there is scotoma and soot and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of phlegm.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it is without power from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And jumping from the wound white moisture resembling pus, and also jumping like charcoal ash;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears to you, then hold back from the treatment, and treat the wound if it is not yet closed;
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the seventh moves as well as the arm, and in court black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	so know without doubt that death is present.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not move is that without plain foam jumping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and gasps loudly and shivers with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and it gives great pain and much sorrow and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound some thing of undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and jumps a point of fiber through the intestine root, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, like the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and thigh and hip and legs, and the seeming member, are safe according to more dispostitions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you do otherwise.
