Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man with an arrow lodged or stuck in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I attempted it, and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and was healed without any feeling at all.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And treat with a tool an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye under the skin.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was replaced, and one could only reach the point towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large as a turquoise bow, all one iron without ears; the tool was sound, and he had no bad accidents from it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And treated an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was the barber, and skillfully as I treated him, he was healed for the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And treated an arrow in a man, that it was in his belly or stomach, and thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and I removed it, and treated the wound, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish a man whose arrow fell or to the back, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural positions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor find annoyance in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you wish another man, whose arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remain thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow in i.e.  a man of the princes the king, that it was lodged among his ribs.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was a little declining to the right side; and the arrow was completely turned around.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the cure after it had been lodged three days. So I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt her with a whole subtle tent, and did not feel her at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And she felt pricking and pain below her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the spot a cataplasm atramentous and digestive, for that the place did not inflame.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the wound of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the plaster on for a few days, and sewed up the wound directly, and so the patient remained for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow still inside his flesh; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicine of acrid corrosion for several days, until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and try it, and feel the head of the arrow that is situated in place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it penetrated well the ends for four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then widened so the wound that I put pliers on it, and mine from one side and the other, and it could not issue out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore do not cease to subtly work and devise instruments, until I took one day pliers well made
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treated it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the masters judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on those things which I do not say, because the books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well very few things, and on those which are present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not from members where they are lodged except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which shoots beyond being in the flesh, it is an arrow entering into the flesh, and shooting no more at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not shoot anymore, then leave it as long as the flesh is sore and inflamed around it,  and make the exit
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is caught in the bone, and it cannot be moved, then leave it thus for several days, and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, pierce around all that is to say a fine forest, until the skin around is enlarged, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is caught in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not treat it, but leave it until it is equal after several days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes as far as the shaft, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not come as far as the shaft,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, if the engine of the teat.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot be pulled out further, then administer turpentine as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is placed back in its place in the body, but it cannot be seen, then try all the ways to remove it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then try to remove it with no suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there are no bones, or nerves, or veins, then widen as much as the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at its base by which it holds.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if bone is caught that is fixed in two parts as much as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and do it carefully so that you don't break the arrow, but rather extract it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then lay him down until his limbs are relaxed, then treat him, for the extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood goes against you, then administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard yourself from cutting the nerve and the vein, and put everything as you can to safely extract the arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and position the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow hit him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, place it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, where one sees or feels nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place if it can be seen.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then upwards, as long as the pliers can take hold, and then extract it; if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow shaft is in it, drive it out with the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft has fallen, and you see administering thrust, administer one instrument pointed;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters the head of the instrument; and then drive it out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged, put one instrument with a point entering it, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is surrounded, you should cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it is necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the hip or belly or bladder or rib, and it is near the surface, and you can cut into it, then cut into it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And keep from cutting the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if need be.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows resembles that of an eye, and behold here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the end of a hair is like the quill of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To put at the tip of an arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pliers to insert and to grasp is this.
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one heals are xxxi., of which it has or head xvi.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: ij. bats that are after the ears, that are called the two "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the ij. arteries that are in ij. temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and ij. veins that are in ij. tear ducts of the ij. eyes, that are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins which are on the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly heals are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic and is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilica,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side of the chest,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is on the bone
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one from which blood is drawn, which opens manifestly over the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphenous vein is the vein between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and where the foot is there are three veins: one of which is below the curve of the pouch on the left side;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called «ness», that is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the veins that are after the ears so helps with old catarrhs, and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck to a vise,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which you then grasp with your hand, and where you feel the pulse under your back, tighten it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and thrust it below the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cover the skin and the vein well two fingers wide, and make blood flow as much as you see
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and bind it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for an old headache,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and quickly, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of the sharp tears to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the blood if it is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulsations under his jawbone, and then takes it in hand;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then gently place the heart above the vein toward your index finger, and push the lancet below.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	And gently lift the vein upwards, and the cup, as you have done in 2 other veins, and make a correct flow of blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then untie the patient, and put your hand over the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form the bandage, and leave it there until it is healed; and we have already spoken about their coping and extraction, as at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood of the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the blood of the cephalic in old facial diseases, and for migraine, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains his neck twisting it, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and steady with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and no time the work of a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it does not suit that the flames are too thick; and the healing across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two tear ducts helps the eyes, and to the ridge, and to the redness, and to the origin in the eye, and to diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with a certain linen, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy, and let the wound be through the, a piece of the length of the flame a piece wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks; then make a correction of the blood, as much as you need, and then tie up cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The wound of the vein of the knee is good for fever, and for sore eyes, and for diseases of the face
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as for migraine and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the bloodletting are such that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose towards your left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and takes a subtle long flame, and inserts it between the lips in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well by itself, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it go too far in depth, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up at night because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the .ij. guindeges helps in the treatment of the spleen, and at the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and itching, and corrosions, and herpes, and scabies;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the blood are that the patient should extract his neck from below both sides as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein of long one a little widely, then draw blood temperately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other side in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and draw all the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and let him lie until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the upper lips helps in collection in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and sores and inflammation.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the blood is to make the sick person sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you recognize them by this that they are black, and by this that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore, do both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you cut the larger of each side, and also make two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein below the tongue helps after the cephalic vein, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the veins are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and raise the tongue, and look under each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then prick one and the other, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which are commonly bled are pricked according to two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either they are pricked at one flame  about as wide as a finger, or with a subtle olive like a sharp cutter, and it is called "aneasil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and fine according to the wideness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very well-known, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the veins that are full of thick blood that appears on the surface and that contain thick and troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so helps with ailments that are below the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and that he should take care of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it behooves him to stanch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be piercing flame, but cutting as a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil does not clearly open, then you should restrain it and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no vein of it, or you open the vein in its place in the arm: it clearly opens;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cauterize with the knife-like flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the joint, then it is fitting thus that you pull out the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place with a mark, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame aniseed;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and guard that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is of the artery: therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten yourself then, and put your foot upon lengthening, then remove your foot if it is without stretching, which many times happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Tie his arm up, and leave it so, and do not let the patient move it; and be on guard, and do not let him move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stretched and it aches, and the medicine is not present, then close the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and stretch the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of fig, and make it into paste, and take one of the halves and tie it well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the wound is clean, that is good; if not, treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not always done in more positions because of the small size of the wound and the possibility of the arm's ligature.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle helps to draw blood from above the head and from below the body,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the physician to lay himself across for the nerve that is below, and if they are not too deeply embedded, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the saints be grievers, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any men for its subtlety, then it is necessary that you heal it with the anesthetic instrument; and  escape the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed by pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because it is the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place and it does not harm if the first time one fails, and one begins again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance inflates the veins in some men, when one fails the first time, but it does not harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is only administered to preserve health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are or cut: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of prayers in spring, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding which is administered to illnesses has no set hour, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not bleed children until fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed those who are over sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the bowels with a light enema,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have a lot of feces retained, so that the veins do not attract impurities from the bowels harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Do not bleed those who are too full of meat, nor who are drunk, until they are sober, nor the dropsy-stricken;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one worsens after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea of the belly, and multiplication of labor in women, and labor, watching, and fasting, and all that the virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly reduce the humors, if it is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have their power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then go into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly thin the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and vein yourself from the lower leg towards the groin, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself free from labor, and from points, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joyful, and let the hands of the healer be higher than those who are healed, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then straighten the linen in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot heal without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the veins with a bit of old oil, then place his finger from his left hand on that vein below its level a bit where he wants to bleed
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the vein be not cut and fail to bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that bleed as thick as cords, and some that are filled with windiness
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the cautery on it, it retracts like a flame and cannot open the vein, and this is how it is with these
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, if the wound is too tight, for that it is necessary that the surgeon be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, he begins again a little below where it was or above, if the place is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is inflamed and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days, and bind not the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for perchance an abscess will come; nor let him enter water, then begin again the vein if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the vein is short and subtle, and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, then fire in that same opening directly to the whole flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little carefully, so that the eyes be inflamed; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place inflamed, then do not begin the bloodletting again, and put on a little bit of olive oil, for it calms the body of blood, and is mixed in this place with the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the olive oil in every bloodletting that you open the veins, to stop the course of the blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and the same thing happens threefold and bows of it when it is placed in its place; so subtle the sinew and it splits when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens often, even when it is not drained except on that time when the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and place on it a sponge moistened in water and some hot oil, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood from the vein has flowed out, and if it remains in place after a few days without any blackness or greenness, then it will not harm it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, put on no thing of aloes or myrrh in juice of calamine, ointment, or semblance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances at the wound of the basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the compression of the hand, so is that appearance bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid that you put on anything of those things we have said, for by chance it cuts without the artery; but make  one plaster dry to harden the place, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And he who is weak and pale, and needs the extraction of blood, should have a wider wound made, and the flames wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him often and little, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this way of bleeding is safe from a decrease in blood and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding from the long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body needs bloodletting, it is necessary to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is faint, treat him with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, give him softened bread before bloodletting in a syrup of figs, or in a syrup of honey aromatic with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during bloodletting, after the issue of some blood, it is necessary that he suck broth of meat, and a subtle aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another place, then he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood within the body that is already exhausted, and brings fever; so in this case, it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it flows in streams.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you have rewarded all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his wrists when he is healthy, that death may not come in place of a parsimonious.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not fitting when you see a limb loosened, and draw blood the second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	but if it is curved, let him extend his arm as far as possible, for this would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it heal until the second time; or you prick it at the tip of the flame, as long as the vein which is frozen will be closed.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on i. bit of wool moistened in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not tighten it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires bleeding a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in place of the vein in the neck because it is composed
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the joint is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now through the middle, neither short nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and be the puncture wide, and bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot flow out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not plunge the hand into hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is safer from all other veins, because there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it is broken crookedly, and if you cut it through completely, it will cause no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not make them too wide apart, for the nerves are all uncovered from flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if it has frozen in the wound and cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and wool on the vein to stop it firmly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of them in the left hand is equal to the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you towards right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The vein of the sphene is equal to all diseases that are below the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as well as diseases of the intestines, and retention of flowers, and diseases of the hips, thighs, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of this vein are that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs over the vein until it throbs,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and tie above the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so take the largest vein then, or at the ankle, that you see it is worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it on the foot, ward off the nerves that are below, and make the cut across as when cutting; and let the flame be untied.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot feel it, put the foot in water, and leave the vein to bleed well open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first incision is necessary, then begin again above a little, because the wound is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and then do the same with the sole of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle, and its incision relieves pain in the hip, when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its incision are that the patient enters or bathes in water and is strained above the ankle four fingers' width by twisting it.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then close it in all ways that you can, and across
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the flesh is dry, and it is very well supplied by the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then close any vein that opens or at the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard against the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make as much bloodletting as you see fit, and then untie the bandage, and put cotton on it and restrain it; she is now cured.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction which is without pricking, it is done in two ways: either with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the suction which is done by pricking and drawing blood, it is done in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely in its head; and the other is in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in two ribs of the neck; and the suction under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the two shoulders; and the suction on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suctions in the two arms; and the suctions on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups on the two ankles; and suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because of this it does not weaken one as much as from opening a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither with hot nor cold fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it is necessary to suction, or for customs, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between, and at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to blow, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and those who bring forth repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who bring forth a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and bleed from the gums.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see through blood and fog and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to vomit after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the vein helps in the greatness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this should be after the evacuation of the whole body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this vomiting is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not fitting for those who are of cold constitution or who have catarrh, because this does great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those who have or chief cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Ventosaion in the neck is in place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and for this reason it is suitable for the treatment of the pain
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the opening of the channel of the peritoneum, and to all kinds of fullness;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and there it is fitting to poke gently, for if it holds too firmly, it obstructs or stomach and or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilations of the two ribs of the neck are worth for pains of the head, and headache and migraine, and in strangulation, and to the pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and it is fitting that you command the patient to express his hand upon putting, that he does not cut the artery, and there comes a hemorrhage.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilations under the chin are worth for mouth disease, and gum decay, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for the illness that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the armpits is as good as three veins in the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the patient not to shave it too much, because the skin is bare of flesh, and shows veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids from the foundation, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and be of iron, that it has need to well milk; and perchance, if it was subtle, it would break; and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are applied openly, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the reins, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and are in their place of two shins, and of two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and succeed temperately, and put it gently, and move evenly, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then firm, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, because there are such who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a prick deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to prick it twice: the first time to make a subtle passage for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only pierce once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we start again often; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it in the middle, and the end so that the skin be pierced carefully.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin and whose pores are closed, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with oil appetizer and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of gourd;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the spring, of cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one whom one heals has tender flesh and wide pores, then it is not fitting to put any oil on them
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash after the aeration of rose water, or cold water, or elderberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, may rise from ash, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or buckthorn water, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And it is not necessary to cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after bathing an hour or two; and do not sleep after the cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he  be warded, when he must be winnowed and when he is winnowed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And ward if the one who is well is choleric, and if his flesh is too much red and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary that he eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the  side, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced pigeons, and roast meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and quince, and quince, and small eels and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he shall fast, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no one at any time garlic or nutmeg before or after the venesection to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle with the wine, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are applied without hurting are those that are put on the liver, and on the mouse, and gout, and on the belly and the bladder and the hips and the groin, because those members do not suffer being hurt on their eyes.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the nipples when they are giving birth; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the bladder to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or displaces the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it is done when one puts it upon the liver and upon the mouse when there is wind retained.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of tepid water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in illnesses of the pleura, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water to which herbs suitable for it have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have 2 fingers wide and half a palm in length, and have or costate around the middle 1 small hole, as for to put a needle
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of iron, soft in front so that it does not burn the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a transverse rod of iron or steel, to put a candle enclosed,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are other than those of old people, and of thin ones than of fat ones
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one thus place this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle wax or .i. liniment, and put it inside the suction cup across from the stem which is inside the suction cup
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame be at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it upon the limb, and these must be on the punctured place that we have said, so that when one wants, so in goes the vapor, and one takes off the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take up the linen as before, and recommence it often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup which is administered in the illness of pleuresin, to all acute [conditions], has no rod nor punctured place, and is not administered further than when it is full of water, and is put upon the limb only as much as;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suctions are not administered except in members where one cannot place cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and their denuded flesh, such as two or three, and other similar parts;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the qualities of the user are that when you find cuppings that are in clear sweet waters without blemish, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them one by one in fresh water until they become accustomed to it and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with leeches and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the poultices.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and softened, if it is their place where one can put a cupping glass, then put it, because this is very helpful after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place with a little bit of water and then very well, and then sprinkle it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too much after the poultices, then moisten one linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the poultice is extinguished;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the abscess is multiplied, put on it powdered vitriol or saltpeter, and similar things, until it is extended.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and let them until they are dried on the place, then it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of it, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the poultices do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or you stick a needle into it until the pus comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them up, and as soon as they feel the blood, they get hot.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, powder them with a little bit of aloe and flaxseed ground together, or ashes, and they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoring of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the fools who read from this chapter will never see any of the ancient books, nor will they ever read them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, knowledge is kept hidden in our land, because I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing else, except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.
